Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Imam al-Sanusi: His Name, Lineage, and Epithets
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi with name, lineage, and epithets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the full name, lineage, tribal affiliation, and key epithets of Imam al-Sanusi, including the meaning of 'al-Tawhidi'.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's epithets reveal his scholarly identity and deep roots in Sunni theology.

This lesson introduces the biography of Imam al-Sanusi, the great Ash'ari theologian. We will learn his full name, his tribal origin from the Sanusa tribe, and why he is called 'al-Tawhidi'. Understanding his background helps us appreciate his contributions to Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the long list of honorifics and nisbas.
2
Identify the nisbas
Find all the relative names (nisbas) in his name: al-Sanusi, al-Tilmisani, al-Maliki, al-Ash'ari, al-Tawhidi. Also note the additional ones from his handwriting.
Each nisba connects him to a tribe, place, school, or specialty.
3
Understand 'al-Sanusi' and 'al-Tawhidi'
Focus on the explanations given: 'al-Sanusi' is from the Sanusa tribe, and 'al-Tawhidi' means he is occupied with the science of tawhid.
This shows his tribal roots and his theological focus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي شيخ متكلمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدّث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي . والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في " تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية » ووجد بخطه على ( شرح الآجرومية ( له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى . والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي
Translation of Imam al-Sanusi: the shaykh of the theologians of his time and his country, the imam, the all-knowing scholar, the hadith specialist, the reciter, the jurist, the fundamentalist investigator, the pious ascetic; Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilmisani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. And al-Sanusi: a relative attribution to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in 'Taj al-Arus': 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi because he settled among them; and it is said he is from them. His mother is a sharifa Hasaniyya.' So verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Mallali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya'. And it was found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I say: al-Isawi: from the house of Isa. And al-Tawhidi: relative attribution to preoccupation with the science of tawhid; so mentioned by al-Hafnawi.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biography (tarjama) of Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by listing his honorifics and his full name: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi, with the nisbas al-Tilmisani (from Tlemcen), al-Maliki (school), al-Ash'ari (theological school), and al-Tawhidi (due to his work in tawhid). It then explains the origin of 'al-Sanusi', attributing it to the Sanusa tribe. It cites al-Zabidi's 'Taj al-Arus' for two opinions: that al-Sanusi settled among them or that he was from them, and that his mother was a sharifa (descendant of the Prophet) from the Hasanid line. It also notes that al-Sanusi wrote in his hand on his Sharh al-Ajrumiyya the nisbas 'al-Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar', and the author comments that 'al-Isawi' means from the house of Isa. Finally, it explains that 'al-Tawhidi' refers to his occupation with the science of tawhid (Islamic theology), citing al-Hafnawi.

Key Terms
السنوسي
التوحيدي
تلمساني
مالكي
أشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Sanusi was named 'al-Tawhidi' because he wrote a book titled 'al-Tawhid'.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that 'al-Tawhidi' is a relative attribution to his preoccupation with the science of tawhid, not to a book title.

Checkpoint
What is the reason for al-Sanusi's epithet 'al-Tawhidi' according to the passage?
A) He wrote a book named al-Tawhid
B) He was from the Tawhid tribe
C) He was preoccupied with the science of tawhid
D) He was a student of al-Tawhidi

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's full name and epithets reflect his scholarly lineage, tribal roots, and dedication to the science of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi was called 'al-Tawhidi' because he was habitually engaged in the science of tawhid. If your daily conversations and thoughts were examined, what 'science' or preoccupation would they reveal you are actually devoted to? Are you comfortable with that label before Allah?
?
His lineage includes tribal, regional, and school affiliations. When you introduce yourself, which identities do you highlight, and do they reflect a genuine commitment to truth or just social pride?
?
The passage mentions that al-Sanusi settled among a tribe and became associated with them. In your community, are you known more for your outward belonging or for your inner devotion to knowledge and worship? What change would make your 'epithet' more truthful?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
Imam al-Sanusi's Name and Nisbas
Biography introduces Imam al-Sanusi's full name and explains his nisbas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Sanusi's full name, epithets, and nisbas establish his scholarly identity and specialization in theology.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's nisbas reveal both his tribal roots and his theological specialization.

In this lesson, we meet Imam al-Sanusi through the classical biographical tradition. The passage introduces his full name, a series of honorific epithets, and explains two of his primary nisbas—al-Sanusi and al-Tawhidi. This establishes his scholarly credentials and lineage in the Sunni tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the long list of titles describing al-Sanusi's expertise.
The epithets cover hadith, fiqh, usul, tasawwuf, etc.
2
Analyze the epithets
Identify each epithet and consider what it tells us about his mastery of different Islamic sciences.
3
Explore 'al-Sanusi' nisba
The author explains it relates to the Sanusa Berber tribe. Note the citation of al-Zabidi and the alternate attribution from al-Mallali.
This nisba links him to a specific tribal lineage.
4
Explore 'al-Tawhidi' nisba
This nisba directly indicates his specialization in the science of tawhid (Islamic theology).
5
Reflect on the purpose
Consider how this biographical introduction sets the stage for a work on theology by establishing the author's authority.
The nisba al-Tawhidi is key—it signals his field.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي
شيخ متكلمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدّث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي .
والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في " تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية (١) ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية (۲) ووجد بخطه على ( شرح الآجرومية ( له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى ((٣)
والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي هذه النسبة له في « تعريف الخلف » (۱)
Translation of Imam al-Sanusi. The master of the theologians of his time and his country, the imam, the all-knowing scholar, the hadith specialist, the reciter, the jurist, the usuli investigator, the Sufi, pious and ascetic; Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilmisani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi.
Al-Sanusi: a relative attribution to Sanusa, a Berber tribe in the Maghrib. Al-Zabidi said in Taj al-Arus: 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi because he settled among them; it is said he is from them. His mother is a sharifa Hasanid (1), similarly verified by Sidi Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Mallali in al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya (2), and found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-Isa al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I say: al-Isa is from the house of Isa (3).
Al-Tawhidi: a relative attribution to occupying oneself with the science of tawhid. Thus al-Hafnawi mentioned this attribution for him in Ta'rif al-Khalaf (1).
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction that first describes Imam al-Sanusi with several epithets highlighting his scholarship in various Islamic sciences (hadith, fiqh, usul, tasawwuf), then explains two of his key nisbas: 'al-Sanusi' and 'al-Tawhidi'. The author provides the origin of 'al-Sanusi' as a relation to the Sanusa tribe, citing al-Zabidi's Taj al-Arus, and adds that his mother was a sharifa from the Hasanids. Then he mentions a different reading from al-Mallali that adds 'al-Isa al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar', and the author comments that 'al-Isa' refers to the house of Isa. The second nisba 'al-Tawhidi' is attributed to his specialization in the science of tawhid (Islamic theology). The passage sets the stage for his scholarly identity by linking him to both a tribal lineage and a theological discipline.

Key Terms
سنوسي
توحيدي
ترجمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The nisba 'al-Sanusi' refers to a place name or a Sufi order.
Correction: It is described as a relation to the Sanusa Berber tribe; al-Sanusi himself is an individual scholar, not a founder of a later order.

Checkpoint
What does the nisba 'al-Tawhidi' indicate?
A) He was from a town called Tawhid
B) He specialized in the science of tawhid
C) He was a follower of the Tawhid sect
D) He wrote a book on tawhid

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's name and nisbas encode his tribal lineage and his dedication to the science of tawhid, establishing his authority as a theologian.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at the titles and nisbas in your own name. Which of them reflect a conscious choice of learning (like 'al-Tawhidi') and which are just inherited? If you had to add one nisba describing your actual specialization, what would it be — and does your life reflect that?
?
Imam al-Sanusi is called 'master of the theologians' and described with many sciences, yet his nisba 'al-Tawhidi' singles out tawhid. Do you treat the knowledge of Allah's attributes as the centerpiece of your practice, or do you let other sciences distract you from the most important subject?
?
The passage notes that al-Sanusi may be from the tribe or just settled among them. Are you known among others by your chosen commitments or only by your unearned affiliations? What would it take for your identity to be more like 'al-Tawhidi' — defined by your devotion to knowing Allah?

The Disputed Birth Year of Imam al-Sanusi
The biographer discusses conflicting reports on Sanusi's birth year and cites al-Tunbukti's account.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the disagreement among early biographers regarding Imam Sanusi's birth year and how a specific report from al-Tunbukti provides one possible calculation.

Core Idea
Sanusi's birth year is not definitively known; early sources conflict.

This passage from a biographical work on Imam al-Sanusi highlights the challenges of reconstructing the lives of early scholars. The author notes a disagreement over al-Sanusi's birth year and cites a report from al-Tunbukti that offers one calculation. As you read, consider how oral transmission and written notes shaped Islamic biographical literature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: it opens with a statement of disagreement, then cites a source, then draws a conclusion.
The passage is short but contains a complete argument.
2
Identify the source of the report
Find where the biographer cites his authority. The report comes from al-Tunbukti's book 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj', which quotes al-Mallali's statement about the shaykh's age.
Notice the chain: al-Tunbukti saw a note from some scholars who asked al-Mallali.
3
Calculate the birth year
Using the report that Sanusi died at age 63, and knowing his death year (895 AH), calculate the birth year. The passage gives 832 AH. Verify the math: 895 - 63 = 832.
This shows how biographers deduced dates from age reports.
4
Reflect on the nature of the disagreement
Consider why there might be conflicting reports. The passage mentions 'lack of certainty' and 'confusion in transmission'. This reflects the limitations of oral history.
Think about how this affects our knowledge of early scholars' lives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مولده ونشأته يرجع لعدم ذلك اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي ; وسبب نصه هو على ذلك واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً ، قال العلامة التُنْبُكْتي في نيل الابتهاج (۲) : ( رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء : أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ ، فقال له : مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة )(٣) فعلى هذه الرواية : تكون السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام السنوسي هي ( ۱۳۲ هـ )
His birth and upbringing: Due to the lack thereof, there is disagreement about the year of birth of Imam al-Sanusi, and the reason for his [the biographer's] text being thus, and the confusion in the transmission of his student al-Mallali regarding that as well. Al-Tunbukti said in Nayl al-Ibtihaj (2): 'I saw a note from some scholars that he asked the aforementioned al-Mallali about the age of the Shaykh, and he said to him: He died at sixty-three years.' (3) So according to this narration, the year in which Imam al-Sanusi was born is 832 AH.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses the disagreement among sources regarding the birth year of Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by stating the problem: there is a lack of certainty, leading to disagreement. It then provides a specific report from al-Tunbukti in his book Nayl al-Ibtihaj, quoting a note that al-Mallali was asked about the Shaykh's age and responded that he died at 63. From this, the biographer deduces that the birth year would be 832 AH (since he died in 895 AH). The passage highlights the reliance on oral transmission and the need to reconcile conflicting reports.

Key Terms
السنوسي
الملالي
التنبكتي
نيل الابتهاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi's birth year is definitively known and agreed upon by all early biographers.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that there is disagreement due to lack of certainty and conflicting reports, and it offers only one possible calculation based on a specific narration.

Checkpoint
According to al-Tunbukti's report, what did al-Mallali say about the age of Imam Sanusi at his death?
A) 55 years
B) 63 years
C) 56 years
D) 65 years

Key Takeaway
The birth year of Imam al-Sanusi is uncertain, with one report from al-Tunbukti suggesting 832 AH based on al-Mallali's statement that he died at age 63.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter conflicting reports about an important figure in Islamic history, how do you decide what to believe? Does this uncertainty unsettle your trust in the tradition?
?
This lesson shows that even a great scholar like Imam al-Sanusi may have a fuzzy birth year. Does that make you more or less comfortable with ambiguity in your own understanding of Islamic knowledge?
?
Imagine you are asked about a significant event in your own life but your memory is faulty. How does this passage challenge you to be humble about historical claims you take for granted?

Imam Sanusi's Pious Father and Family Background
Description of Sanusi's pious father, lineage, and character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pious family environment in which Imam al-Sanusi was raised, including his father's character, lineage, and occupation, and how this shaped his early education.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's upbringing in a house of virtue and knowledge laid the foundation for his later scholarship.

Imam al-Sanusi's early life is not just a biography; it reveals the spiritual and intellectual soil from which his great work grew. In this lesson, you will read the description of his father, Shaykh Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, and learn about the pious atmosphere that surrounded the young Sanusi. This background helps us appreciate the tradition from which the 'Umm al-Barahin emerged.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to get the overall picture of the father's background.
Notice the footnote indicators (1), (2), (3) which refer to additional details.
2
Examine the father's character description
Focus on al-Mallali's quote describing the father's virtues: righteousness, asceticism, humility, good character, and cheerful demeanor.
The father is portrayed as a model of piety and learning.
3
Understand the lineage detail
Identify the term 'al-Hasani' and note that Sanusi's Hasanid lineage comes from his paternal grandmother, not directly from Imam Hasan.
This clarifies a common misconception about his nisba.
4
Reflect on the father's occupation and spiritual state
The father taught Qur'an to children, and divine care accompanied him with miracles and insight. Consider how this environment influenced Sanusi's early education.
This shows the transmission of knowledge and spirituality in the family.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم ; فوالده هو الشيخ الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب 1 ، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها ، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنية النسب ، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه (۲) ، وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام : ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه . . رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً ، خاشعاً الله تعالى ، زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها ، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى ، سالم الصدر ، حسن الأخلاق ، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه ، حسن المعاشرة ، كريم الطبع )(٣) وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب ، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أن عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته ، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته
Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a house of virtue and knowledge; his father is the righteous, ascetic, humble, investigating professor Yusuf Abu Ya'qub 1, and from him the Imam learned the principles of the sciences. That was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge at that time, and the clay of saints and righteous people. The grandmother of Imam al-Sanusi on his father's side was of Hasanid lineage, so the Imam is sometimes called al-Hasani on account of his paternal grandmother. (2) Al-Mallali said in describing the Imam's father: 'My master Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son… he was a righteous, devout man, humble before Allah, ascetic in the world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to Allah, pure of heart, good in character, smiling at everyone he met, good in companionship, noble in nature.' (3) The occupation of this blessed father was teaching the Qur'an to children in the school. From al-Mallali's words, it appears that divine care accompanied him from his childhood, so Allah granted through him miracles and opened his insight.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage describes the family background of Imam al-Sanusi, emphasizing his upbringing in a household of virtue and knowledge. It mentions his father, Shaykh Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, a respected scholar and teacher, from whom Sanusi learned the basics of the sciences in Tlemcen, a city known for its learning and saints. The text also notes that Sanusi's paternal grandmother was of Hasanid descent (descendants of Imam Hasan), hence Sanusi is sometimes called 'al-Hasani'. A lengthy description from al-Mallali portrays the father as righteous, ascetic, humble, good-natured, and cheerful, devoted to worship. His profession was teaching Qur'an to children in a maktab. The passage further suggests that divine grace accompanied him, leading to miraculous occurrences and enlightenment. This biographical detail highlights the pious environment that shaped the young Sanusi.

Key Terms
يوسف أبو يعقوب
الحسني
الملالي
تلمسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Sanusi's 'Husni' lineage indicates a direct patrilineal descent from Imam Hasan.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the lineage comes from his paternal grandmother, not a direct paternal line. Hence, 'al-Hasani' is a secondary nisba.

Checkpoint
What was the occupation of Imam Sanusi's father?
A) Judge (qadi)
B) Teaching Qur'an to children in a school
C) Sufi mystic
D) Merchant

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi was raised by a righteous, ascetic father who taught him the principles of science and provided a spiritually rich environment conducive to his future scholarly and spiritual achievements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your father or mentor: what is the single quality from Yusuf al-Sanusi's character that you feel most lacking in yourself? Would your family describe you as 'smiling at everyone you meet'? If not, what would it take for you to become that person starting today?
?
This passage shows that the prophet's grandson's lineage (Hasanid) was transmitted through a woman (grandmother). How often do you think of the women in your own lineage as carriers of your family's Islamic heritage? Write one concrete action you will take this week to honor a woman in your family who has passed down iman to you.
?
The father's occupation was teaching the Qur'an to children in a humble school. If you were to be completely honest with yourself, do you secretly seek fame or recognition in your Islamic work? In your next act of service, deliberately do it in a way that no one will know it was you. Will you?

Imam Sanusi's Teachers and Expertise in Qira'at
Listing Sanusi's teachers and his high standing in qira'at.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of Imam Sanusi's traditional education and his particular distinction in Quranic recitations (qira'at).

Core Idea
Sanusi's scholarly authority was built on elite teachers and mastery of qira'at.

This brief passage gives us a window into Imam Sanusi's scholarly formation. It tells us that he studied under the leading scholars of his time and that he was especially distinguished in the field of Quranic recitations. Understanding this helps us appreciate the depth of his credentials before we examine his theological works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how concisely it presents two key facts: his teachers and his specialty.
2
Identify the two main points
The passage makes two distinct claims. First, that Sanusi studied under the great scholars of his time and received spiritual care. Second, that he had high standing in qira'at. Identify both.
This is a common structure in biographical notices.
3
Reflect on why this matters
Ask yourself: Why would a kalam theologian begin his biography by highlighting qira'at expertise? This shows his grounding in the Quranic sciences, which underpins his theological authority.
Consider how this connects to the broader aim of the coursebook.

شيوخه · أخذ الإمام السنوسي العلم عن جلَّة علماء عصره ، ونالته عناية ولحظات الأولياء والصالحين · وكان للإمام السنوسي علو كعب في جمع القراءات
His shaykhs: Imam al-Sanusi acquired knowledge from the greats of the scholars of his time, and he received the care and glances of the saints and righteous. Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the compilation of Quranic recitations.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This short passage, under the heading 'His Shaykhs', summarizes the breadth of Sanusi's education. It states that he studied under the leading scholars of his era and was also the object of attention from saints and righteous people, indicating both formal scholarship and spiritual care. It then highlights his particular distinction in the field of qira'at (Quranic recitations), noting that he had a high rank in 'jami' al-qira'at' (the compilation/knowledge of the various recitations). This points to his specialization in this discipline, which was a hallmark of his scholarly profile.

Imam Sanusi's Lineage and His Father's Virtues
Describes Imam Sanusi's lineage and his father's piety and occupation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the noble lineage and pious background of Imam Sanusi, including his father's virtues and occupation.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's father was a model of piety, humility, and devotion.

Before studying Imam Sanusi's theological works, it is valuable to know the virtuous family he came from. This passage introduces his Hasanid lineage through his paternal grandmother and describes his father's character and occupation. It sets the stage for understanding the spiritual environment that shaped the Imam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the mention of lineage and the detailed description of the father's qualities.
2
Identify the lineage detail
The passage explains that Imam Sanusi's Hasanid lineage comes through his paternal grandmother. This is a key point to avoid misunderstanding about his descent.
This clarifies why he is sometimes called al-Hasani.
3
Examine the father's virtues
The description from al-Mallali lists many virtues: righteousness, devotion, asceticism, good character, etc. List each virtue mentioned.
These virtues reflect the Islamic ideal of a pious person.
4
Consider the father's occupation and spiritual gifts
The father taught Qur'an to children, showing his dedication to religious education. The passage also mentions that miraculous events (karamat) occurred at his hands and he had spiritual insight (kashf).
This suggests a blessed family line that contributed to the Imam's own spiritual stature.

وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنية النسب ، ولذا قد يلقب (۲) الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه (٢) ، وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام : ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه . . رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً ، خاشعاً الله تعالى ، زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها ، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى ، سالم الصدر ، حسن الأخلاق ، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه ، حسن المعاشرة ، كريم الطبع )(٣) وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب ، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أن عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته ، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته
His paternal grandmother's lineage was Hasanid, so Imam Sanusi is sometimes called al-Hasani through his father's mother. And al-Shaykh al-Mallali said describing the Imam's father: 'Sayyidi Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son, was a righteous, devout man, humble before Allah, ascetic in the world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to Allah, pure of heart, good in character, smiling at everyone he met, of good companionship, noble in nature.' And the occupation of this blessed father was teaching the Qur'an to children in the school. And from al-Mallali's words it appears that Allah's care accompanied him from childhood, so Allah brought about miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight.

Commentary
This passage provides background on Imam Sanusi's family, specifically his paternal grandmother's Hasanid lineage and his father's virtues. It combines genealogy and hagiography to establish the Imam's noble descent and the piety of his father, Yusuf al-Sanusi. The description from al-Mallali emphasizes the father's asceticism, good character, and humility. His occupation as a Qur'an teacher underscores his religious dedication. The passage also hints at the father's spiritual gifts ('karaamat' and 'kashf'), suggesting a blessed lineage that contributed to the Imam's own spiritual stature.

Sanusi's Teachers and the Seven Qira'at
Details Sanusi's teachers and seven qira'at transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage through which Imam Sanusi learned the seven Qur'anic readings and the rigorous nature of classical Islamic education.

Core Idea
Sanusi's authority in Qur'anic recitation rests on a meticulous chain of master teachers.

Imam Sanusi's education was not merely academic; it was a spiritual and scholarly journey under the greatest minds of his time. This passage traces his training, especially in the seven canonical Qur'anic readings (qira'at), listing teachers who personally recited and authorized him. By examining this chain, we see the high standards of transmission in classical Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first teacher
Read the opening line to see who Sanusi studied foundational sciences with. Notice the description: 'righteous, ascetic, humble, verifying teacher.'
Yusuf Abu Ya'qub is mentioned briefly.
2
Understand the general context
The next sentence states that Sanusi learned from the great scholars of his time and received care from saints. This sets the tone for the detailed chain that follows.
3
Follow the chain for the seven qira'at
Abu Ja'far al-Balawi reports the specific teachers: al-Hasani, then al-Yaznasni and al-Lijai. Note the methods used (recitation in two complete rounds, compilation, authorization).
This chain is the core of the passage.
4
List additional scholars
The passage ends by naming a few more teachers (Nasr al-Zawawi, Muhammad ibn Tumart). Consider why these names are included even though the text cuts off.
The text has a footnote warning about confusing this Muhammad ibn Tumart with the Almohad founder.

للسبع
ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر الزواوي ، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي والشيخ (۲)
(1) The righteous, ascetic, humble, verifying teacher Yusuf Abu Ya'qub 1, from him the Imam took the principles of the sciences 6.
His teachers:
·
Imam al-Sanusi took knowledge from the great scholars of his time, and he received the care and glances of the saints and righteous.
Al-Allama Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: (He took the seven readings from the jurist, teacher, scholar, practitioner, verifier, reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: I added from the third a sufficient amount, the end of which I have not now verified, as a compilation of the seven according to the content of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he authorized him in the seven readings and in other of his narrations with a general absolute authorization. And he narrated to him the seven from the two noble, learned, teaching imams: the great, most famous, most well-known, verifying reciter, the most aware, humble Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi Imran Musa al-Yaznasni, and the great, venerated, famous, verifying, precise, accurate, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, pure Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Faqih al-Alim al-Mutafannin Abi Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Isa al-Lijai, reading to the first as a compilation in a complete recitation of the seven, he said: I added three portions from Sura al-Baqara, and to the second for al-Fatiha and al-Baqara and the beginnings of Al Imran as a compilation, and an authorization for what he read and what remained. They both narrated to him together that from the two teachers: Abu Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut by their chains. (1) For the seven.
And from among the scholars upon whom he read: al-Shaykh al-Allama Nasr al-Zawawi, and al-Shaykh al-Alim Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sinhaji, and al-Shaykh (2).
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage documents Imam Sanusi's scholarly training, focusing on his teachers and his mastery of the seven canonical Qur'anic readings (qira'at). It begins by mentioning his foundational studies with Yusuf Abu Ya'qub. Then it lists the great scholars of his era from whom he acquired knowledge, emphasizing the spiritual care he received from saints. The core of the passage is a meticulous chain of transmission for the seven qira'at, attributed to Abu Ja'far al-Balawi. It details specific teachers: Abu al-Hajjaj al-Hasani, then via al-Yaznasni and al-Lijai, and further back to al-Qaysi and Ibn Makhkhut. The careful listing of names and methods (recitation, authorization) illustrates the rigor of classical Islamic education. The passage also names additional scholars under whom Sanusi read, such as Nasr al-Zawawi and Muhammad ibn Tumart, though the text trails off. This establishes Sanusi's authoritative credentials in Qur'anic recitation.

Correction: The footnote clarifies that this Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sinhaji is a different person, a scholar, not the Almohad leader.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about Sanusi's painstaking journey to authenticate Qur'anic recitation through multiple master teachers and complete recitations. Now ask yourself: when you seek knowledge about your faith, do you chase after shortcuts, or do you invest the time to learn from qualified teachers with living chains? What is one area where you have settled for ‘a little’ when you could have sought depth?
?
The passage describes Sanusi's teachers as 'righteous, ascetic, humble, verifying' and 'the most aware, humble'. These are not just academic degrees—they are spiritual qualities. Look at your own teachers and mentors: do you prioritize someone's character and connection with Allah over their credentials? More importantly, are you seeking to become someone who embodies these qualities as you learn?
?

If your knowledge of the Qur'an is based on mere reading without a careful chain of transmission from recognized masters, what will be your answer? Today, what step can you take to ensure your recitation and understanding are built on solid, transmitted knowledge?

Al-Sanusi's Study of the Seven Qira'at
Chain of teachers for the seven Quranic readings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the chain of teachers through whom al-Sanusi acquired the seven Quranic readings and the nature of his authorization.

Core Idea
The seven readings were transmitted through a meticulous chain of verifiers and reciters.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage, which details al-Sanusi's rigorous training in the seven Quranic readings (qira'at sab'). You will see the names of his teachers, the method of recitation, and the authorizations he received, reflecting the high standards of Quranic transmission in his era.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main teacher for qira'at
Notice that Abu Ja'far al-Balawi is mentioned as the primary teacher from whom al-Sanusi took the seven readings.
Al-Balawi is described with multiple honorifics emphasizing his authority.
2
Trace the chain of transmission
The passage lists two intermediate teachers (al-Yaznasni and al-Lijai) who taught the reciters al-Qaysi and Ibn Makhkhuw. This shows the isnad for the readings.
The chain is: al-Sanusi ← al-Balawi ← al-Yaznasni/al-Lijai ← al-Qaysi/Ibn Makhkhuw.
3
Note the method and authorization
Observe that al-Sanusi recited complete recitations (khatmat) and combined readings from 'al-Taysir' and 'al-Shatibiyya'. He received a general absolute authorization (ijaza mutlaqa).
This ijaza allowed him to transmit the readings and other narrations.

العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية » وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة « البقرة » ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب ) و ( البقرة ( وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما .
للسبع
ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر الزواوي ، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي والشيخ الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو « وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ) الإرشاد ( الإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد . واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ( الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات
وغيرها .
وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن
مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد
The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi: (He took the seven readings (al-qira'at al-sab') from the jurist, the professor, the scholar, the practitioner, the verifier, the reciter Abi al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: I added from the third a sufficient amount whose extent I have not now verified, combining the seven according to the content of 'al-Taysir' and 'al-Shatibiyya'. And he authorized him in the seven recitations and in other narrations of his with a general absolute authorization. And he narrated to him the seven from the two imams, the scholars, the teachers: the noble professor, the most renowned, the reciter, the verifier, the most perspicacious, the humble, Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi Imran Musa al-Yaznasni, and the noble professor, the venerated, the famous, the verifier, the precise, the master, the grammarian, the linguist, the memorizer, the righteous, the purest, Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Faqih al-Alim al-Mutafannin Abi Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Isa al-Lijai. He recited to the first a combined recitation for the seven, he said: I added three parts from Surat al-Baqara, and to the second for Surat al-Fatiha and al-Baqara and the beginnings of Al Imran combined, and an authorization for what he recited and what remained. Both together narrated to him that from the two professors: Abi Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abi al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhuw through their chain. For the seven. And among the scholars from whom he studied: the scholar, the commentator Nasr al-Zawawi, and the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, and the noble sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani; he took from him the seven readings. And the shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab; he took from him jurisprudence. And the equitable scholar Abu Abd Allah al-Habbak; he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And the imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani; he studied under him principles (usul), logic (mantiq), eloquence (bayan), and jurisprudence (fiqh). And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother; he studied under him al-Risala. And he studied—and he and this brother studied under the pious, righteous imam Abi al-Qasim al-Kanabishi—al-Irshad of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of monotheism (ilm al-tawhid). And he occupied himself with narration (riwaya) and the sciences of tradition (ulum al-athar) under the pious, righteous imam Abi Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi. He narrated from him the two Sahihs and other books of hadith and tradition, and he authorized him with what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat and others. And he studied inheritance calculations (fara'id) and arithmetic (hisab) under the noble scholar Abi al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he authorized him with all that he narrates. Likewise, Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif authorized him from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account detailing the numerous teachers from whom the subject (likely Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi) acquired knowledge across various Islamic sciences. It begins with a detailed chain for the seven Quranic readings (qira'at sab'), tracing back through Abu Ja'far al-Balawi to multiple masters, including the reciters Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani and the two professors al-Yaznasni and al-Lijai. The passage notes that al-Sanusi combined readings from al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya and received general authorization (ijaza mutlaqa). The second part lists other scholars under whom he studied: for qira'at (again from al-Hasani), for fiqh (al-Maghili), for astronomy (al-Habbak), for usul, logic, bayan, and fiqh (al-Tilimsani), for the Risala of Ibn Abi Zayd (al-Taluti), for al-Irshad and tawhid (al-Kanabishi), for hadith and riwaya (al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the Sahihs and other works, and who gave him ijaza and samaa'), and for fara'id and hisab (al-Qalasadi). The passage concludes by mentioning another ijaza from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif via his father. The structure is enumerative, listing each teacher and the subject studied. The biographical nature shows the breadth of traditional Islamic education, encompassing Quranic recitation, jurisprudence, theology, logic, hadith, astronomy, and inheritance law.

List of teachers and subjects studied

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi studied under multiple specialists covering a wide range of Islamic disciplines.

After focusing on the seven readings, the passage expands to list other teachers from whom al-Sanusi acquired knowledge in various fields. This lesson surveys those teachers and the sciences they taught, highlighting the comprehensive traditional education that shaped al-Sanusi as a scholar.

The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi: (He took the seven readings (al-qira'at al-sab') from the jurist, the professor, the scholar, the practitioner, the verifier, the reciter Abi al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: I added from the third a sufficient amount whose extent I have not now verified, combining the seven according to the content of 'al-Taysir' and 'al-Shatibiyya'. And he authorized him in the seven recitations and in other narrations of his with a general absolute authorization. And he narrated to him the seven from the two imams, the scholars, the teachers: the noble professor, the most renowned, the reciter, the verifier, the most perspicacious, the humble, Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi Imran Musa al-Yaznasni, and the noble professor, the venerated, the famous, the verifier, the precise, the master, the grammarian, the linguist, the memorizer, the righteous, the purest, Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Faqih al-Alim al-Mutafannin Abi Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Isa al-Lijai. He recited to the first a combined recitation for the seven, he said: I added three parts from Surat al-Baqara, and to the second for Surat al-Fatiha and al-Baqara and the beginnings of Al Imran combined, and an authorization for what he recited and what remained. Both together narrated to him that from the two professors: Abi Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abi al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhuw through their chain. For the seven. And among the scholars from whom he studied: the scholar, the commentator Nasr al-Zawawi, and the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, and the noble sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani; he took from him the seven readings. And the shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab; he took from him jurisprudence. And the equitable scholar Abu Abd Allah al-Habbak; he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And the imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani; he studied under him principles (usul), logic (mantiq), eloquence (bayan), and jurisprudence (fiqh). And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother; he studied under him al-Risala. And he studied—and he and this brother studied under the pious, righteous imam Abi al-Qasim al-Kanabishi—al-Irshad of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of monotheism (ilm al-tawhid). And he occupied himself with narration (riwaya) and the sciences of tradition (ulum al-athar) under the pious, righteous imam Abi Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi. He narrated from him the two Sahihs and other books of hadith and tradition, and he authorized him with what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat and others. And he studied inheritance calculations (fara'id) and arithmetic (hisab) under the noble scholar Abi al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he authorized him with all that he narrates. Likewise, Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif authorized him from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account detailing the numerous teachers from whom the subject (likely Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi) acquired knowledge across various Islamic sciences. It begins with a detailed chain for the seven Quranic readings (qira'at sab'), tracing back through Abu Ja'far al-Balawi to multiple masters, including the reciters Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani and the two professors al-Yaznasni and al-Lijai. The passage notes that al-Sanusi combined readings from al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya and received general authorization (ijaza mutlaqa). The second part lists other scholars under whom he studied: for qira'at (again from al-Hasani), for fiqh (al-Maghili), for astronomy (al-Habbak), for usul, logic, bayan, and fiqh (al-Tilimsani), for the Risala of Ibn Abi Zayd (al-Taluti), for al-Irshad and tawhid (al-Kanabishi), for hadith and riwaya (al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the Sahihs and other works, and who gave him ijaza and samaa'), and for fara'id and hisab (al-Qalasadi). The passage concludes by mentioning another ijaza from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif via his father. The structure is enumerative, listing each teacher and the subject studied. The biographical nature shows the breadth of traditional Islamic education, encompassing Quranic recitation, jurisprudence, theology, logic, hadith, astronomy, and inheritance law.

Sanusi's Early Teachers: Quran, Fiqh, and the Sciences
Sanusi's first teachers and subjects studied.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Sanusi's early education, including Quranic readings, jurisprudence, logic, and theology as taught by his first masters.

Core Idea
Sanusi mastered multiple sciences from diverse teachers early on.

This passage begins the biographical account by naming the first teachers from whom Imam al-Sanusi learned foundational Islamic sciences. From the seven Quranic readings to jurisprudence, logic, and theology, Sanusi sought knowledge from the leading scholars of his time. Read on to see the impressive list of his early mentors.

Guided Path

As you read the passage, note the name of each teacher and the specific science or book they taught Sanusi. This is a list format, so tracking each pair is essential.
There are six teachers mentioned in this passage.

Observe the variety of sciences

Sanusi even studied with his maternal brother.

الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو « وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ) الإرشاد ( الإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد . واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ( الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد (۱) ذكر ذلك العلامة محمد مخلوف في شجرة النور الزكية ) ( ٣٨٧/١ ) . وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ) فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٩٩٩/٢ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي ) ١٥ قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبركان»، و والإمام شيخنا أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه ، وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه أبي عبد الله الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
The noble Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani: he (Sanusi) took from him the seven Quranic readings. And Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab: he took from him jurisprudence. And the upright scholar Abu Abdullah al-Habbak: he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani: he read with him usul (principles of jurisprudence), logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence. And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother: he read with him the 'Risala' (of Ibn Abi Zayd?), and he and his brother read with the pious Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid (theology). And he occupied himself with transmission and the sciences of athar (hadith) under the pious Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, so he narrated from him the 'Sahihayn' (the two Sahihs) and other hadith and athar books, and he (al-Tha'alibi) granted him ijaza (authorization) for what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat (chains of transmission with a special feature) and other things. And he read inheritance law and calculation under the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him ijaza for everything he narrates, and also Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif granted him ijaza on the authority of his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. (1) The scholar Muhammad Makhluq mentioned that in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fahras al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: 'He had a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of primacy, the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, the handshake, the interlacing of fingers, wearing the patchwork cloak, giving the prayer beads, and the instillation of dhikr via his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.' 15. The scholar al-Balawi said: 'And he (Sanusi) took from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah, the righteous Imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan'; and our shaykh Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him; and others. And he also took from Ibn Marzuq, our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the jurist Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the great jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar'; I think he took from him. And he took the science of calculation and inheritance from the eminent jurist in these two fields Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his aforementioned brother. And from these are those whom his student, our companion, the great accomplished blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali, included in the book 'al-Ta'rif bihi' (the introduction to him).'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account listing the teachers from whom Imam al-Sanusi studied various Islamic sciences and the authorizations he received. It begins by naming the first teacher, Abu al-Hajjaj, from whom he learned the seven Quranic readings. Then it mentions Shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Maghili for fiqh, Abu Abdullah al-Habbak for the astrolabe, and Imam al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh. Next, his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti taught him the 'Risala' (likely of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani), and both brothers read with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of al-Juwayni and theology. The passage then describes his engagement with hadith transmission under Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and other works, and received ijaza (authorization to teach and transmit). He also studied inheritance and accounting with Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who granted him ijaza, as did Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif. After that comes a footnote from the editor (Muhammad Makhluq and al-Kattani) providing additional information on Sanusi's general ijaza from al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and mentioning a small register of hadith chains. Finally, the passage cites al-Balawi, who adds more teachers: Abu Ali al-Ahsan ('Abarkan'), Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Jallab, al-Gharabili, and Ibn Tumart for calculation and inheritance. The passage ends by noting that these teachers were collected by his student al-Mallali in a biography. The overall structure is a cumulative list, with the author's main text followed by a footnote and a quotation, all serving to establish Sanusi's credentials and the breadth of his education.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi specialized only in theology (tawhid).
Correction: This lesson shows that his early studies included Quranic readings, jurisprudence, logic, rhetoric, astronomy, and much more, demonstrating a broad curriculum.

Sanusi's Hadith Studies and Ijaza
Sanusi's studies in hadith and transmission with al-Tha'alibi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Sanusi engaged in hadith transmission, including his study with al-Tha'alibi, narrating the Sahihayn, and receiving ijaza and musalsalat.

Core Idea
Sanusi became a transmitter of hadith through direct study and authorization.

After covering the early sciences, the passage now focuses on Sanusi's dedication to hadith (prophetic traditions) and transmission (riwaya). He studied under the renowned scholar Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and received formal authorization (ijaza). Let's examine this part of his scholarly journey.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on hadith studies
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the key terms: al-riwaya, al-athar, al-Tha'alibi, al-Sahihayn, ijaza, musalsalat.
2
Understand the concept of ijaza
Ijaza is a formal permission to transmit hadith or teach books. Here, al-Tha'alibi granted Sanusi ijaza for what he himself could transmit.
3
Note the musalsalat
These are hadith with a special chain feature, like 'firstness' or 'handshake'. Sanusi heard these from al-Tha'alibi.

الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو « وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ) الإرشاد ( الإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد . واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ( الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد (۱) ذكر ذلك العلامة محمد مخلوف في شجرة النور الزكية ) ( ٣٨٧/١ ) . وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ) فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٩٩٩/٢ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي ) ١٥ قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبركان»، و والإمام شيخنا أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه ، وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه أبي عبد الله الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
The noble Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani: he (Sanusi) took from him the seven Quranic readings. And Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab: he took from him jurisprudence. And the upright scholar Abu Abdullah al-Habbak: he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani: he read with him usul (principles of jurisprudence), logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence. And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother: he read with him the 'Risala' (of Ibn Abi Zayd?), and he and his brother read with the pious Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid (theology). And he occupied himself with transmission and the sciences of athar (hadith) under the pious Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, so he narrated from him the 'Sahihayn' (the two Sahihs) and other hadith and athar books, and he (al-Tha'alibi) granted him ijaza (authorization) for what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat (chains of transmission with a special feature) and other things. And he read inheritance law and calculation under the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him ijaza for everything he narrates, and also Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif granted him ijaza on the authority of his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. (1) The scholar Muhammad Makhluq mentioned that in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fahras al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: 'He had a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of primacy, the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, the handshake, the interlacing of fingers, wearing the patchwork cloak, giving the prayer beads, and the instillation of dhikr via his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.' 15. The scholar al-Balawi said: 'And he (Sanusi) took from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah, the righteous Imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan'; and our shaykh Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him; and others. And he also took from Ibn Marzuq, our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the jurist Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the great jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar'; I think he took from him. And he took the science of calculation and inheritance from the eminent jurist in these two fields Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his aforementioned brother. And from these are those whom his student, our companion, the great accomplished blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali, included in the book 'al-Ta'rif bihi' (the introduction to him).'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account listing the teachers from whom Imam al-Sanusi studied various Islamic sciences and the authorizations he received. It begins by naming the first teacher, Abu al-Hajjaj, from whom he learned the seven Quranic readings. Then it mentions Shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Maghili for fiqh, Abu Abdullah al-Habbak for the astrolabe, and Imam al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh. Next, his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti taught him the 'Risala' (likely of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani), and both brothers read with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of al-Juwayni and theology. The passage then describes his engagement with hadith transmission under Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and other works, and received ijaza (authorization to teach and transmit). He also studied inheritance and accounting with Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who granted him ijaza, as did Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif. After that comes a footnote from the editor (Muhammad Makhluq and al-Kattani) providing additional information on Sanusi's general ijaza from al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and mentioning a small register of hadith chains. Finally, the passage cites al-Balawi, who adds more teachers: Abu Ali al-Ahsan ('Abarkan'), Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Jallab, al-Gharabili, and Ibn Tumart for calculation and inheritance. The passage ends by noting that these teachers were collected by his student al-Mallali in a biography. The overall structure is a cumulative list, with the author's main text followed by a footnote and a quotation, all serving to establish Sanusi's credentials and the breadth of his education.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi became an authorized transmitter of hadith, narrating the Sahihayn and receiving ijaza from al-Tha'alibi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you study the teachings of Islam, do you know the chain of transmission from the Prophet to you? How does Sanusi's dedication to authentic transmission challenge you to verify and prioritize sources in your own learning?
?
Sanusi did not merely study hadith; he received a formal ijaza to teach and transmit. Are you content to be a passive consumer of Islamic knowledge, or will you seek direct connections with qualified teachers and strive to become a transmitter of what you learn?
?
The ijaza represents a living link to the past. What practical steps will you take to ensure that the knowledge you acquire is not just academic but transmitted through a living tradition of teacher-student relationships?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Sanusi's Study of Inheritance and Calculation
Sanusi's studies in inheritance and arithmetic with al-Qalasadi and Ibn Marzuq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's studies in inheritance law (fara'id) and calculation (hisab) under al-Qalasadi and Ibn Marzuq, including the ijaza he received.

Core Idea
Sanusi mastered applied sciences through renowned mathematicians.

The passage now moves to Sanusi's studies in the practical sciences of inheritance (fara'id) and arithmetic (hisab). He studied under the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, a famous mathematician, and also received ijaza from Ibn Marzuq. This demonstrates that Sanusi's education was not limited to religious sciences but included mathematical disciplines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teachers and subjects
The passage mentions two teachers: al-Qalasadi for fara'id and hisab, and Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif who also granted ijaza.
Note the names and honorifics.
2
Understand the significance of ijaza in practical sciences
Like hadith, ijaza was also given for teaching mathematical sciences, indicating a formal mastery.

الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو « وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ) الإرشاد ( الإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد . واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ( الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد (۱) ذكر ذلك العلامة محمد مخلوف في شجرة النور الزكية ) ( ٣٨٧/١ ) . وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ) فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٩٩٩/٢ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي ) ١٥ قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبركان»، و والإمام شيخنا أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه ، وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه أبي عبد الله الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
The noble Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani: he (Sanusi) took from him the seven Quranic readings. And Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab: he took from him jurisprudence. And the upright scholar Abu Abdullah al-Habbak: he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani: he read with him usul (principles of jurisprudence), logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence. And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother: he read with him the 'Risala' (of Ibn Abi Zayd?), and he and his brother read with the pious Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid (theology). And he occupied himself with transmission and the sciences of athar (hadith) under the pious Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, so he narrated from him the 'Sahihayn' (the two Sahihs) and other hadith and athar books, and he (al-Tha'alibi) granted him ijaza (authorization) for what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat (chains of transmission with a special feature) and other things. And he read inheritance law and calculation under the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him ijaza for everything he narrates, and also Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif granted him ijaza on the authority of his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. (1) The scholar Muhammad Makhluq mentioned that in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fahras al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: 'He had a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of primacy, the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, the handshake, the interlacing of fingers, wearing the patchwork cloak, giving the prayer beads, and the instillation of dhikr via his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.' 15. The scholar al-Balawi said: 'And he (Sanusi) took from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah, the righteous Imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan'; and our shaykh Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him; and others. And he also took from Ibn Marzuq, our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the jurist Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the great jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar'; I think he took from him. And he took the science of calculation and inheritance from the eminent jurist in these two fields Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his aforementioned brother. And from these are those whom his student, our companion, the great accomplished blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali, included in the book 'al-Ta'rif bihi' (the introduction to him).'

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account listing the teachers from whom Imam al-Sanusi studied various Islamic sciences and the authorizations he received. It begins by naming the first teacher, Abu al-Hajjaj, from whom he learned the seven Quranic readings. Then it mentions Shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Maghili for fiqh, Abu Abdullah al-Habbak for the astrolabe, and Imam al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh. Next, his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti taught him the 'Risala' (likely of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani), and both brothers read with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of al-Juwayni and theology. The passage then describes his engagement with hadith transmission under Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and other works, and received ijaza (authorization to teach and transmit). He also studied inheritance and accounting with Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who granted him ijaza, as did Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif. After that comes a footnote from the editor (Muhammad Makhluq and al-Kattani) providing additional information on Sanusi's general ijaza from al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and mentioning a small register of hadith chains. Finally, the passage cites al-Balawi, who adds more teachers: Abu Ali al-Ahsan ('Abarkan'), Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Jallab, al-Gharabili, and Ibn Tumart for calculation and inheritance. The passage ends by noting that these teachers were collected by his student al-Mallali in a biography. The overall structure is a cumulative list, with the author's main text followed by a footnote and a quotation, all serving to establish Sanusi's credentials and the breadth of his education.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you acquire religious knowledge, do you actively seek formal authorization or verification from qualified teachers to ensure its accurate transmission? What steps will you take this week to anchor your learning in a reliable chain?
?

In what area of your daily life—whether finances, family duties, or personal habits—are you tempted to be careless despite Allah's command for justice? Write down one concrete action you will take tomorrow to align with that justice.

Additional Teachers and Ijazat: Sanusi's Broad Network
Additional teachers and ijazat, including a list by al-Balawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional teachers and authorizations Sanusi received, as documented by later scholars, including the list of his shuyukh compiled by his student.

Core Idea
Sanusi's scholarly network extended through many ijazat and teachers.

The passage concludes with supplementary information from later biographers: al-Makhluq and al-Kattani mention Sanusi's general ijaza from key teachers, and al-Balawi provides a list of additional shuyukh from Sanusi's own town. This shows how his student al-Mallali compiled a full biography. Let's explore these final details.

Guided Path
1
Read the footnotes and additional quotes
The text includes comments from later scholars (Muhammad Makhluq, al-Kattani) and a quote from al-Balawi. Note the names of additional teachers.
2
Identify the general ijaza and the register
Al-Kattani mentions Sanusi had a general ijaza and a small register of hadith chains. Understand that this was common for traveling scholars.
3
See the compilation by al-Mallali
Sanusi's student compiled a biography (al-Ta'rif bihi) that includes these teachers.
