الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو « وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ) الإرشاد ( الإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد . واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ( الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد (۱) ذكر ذلك العلامة محمد مخلوف في شجرة النور الزكية ) ( ٣٨٧/١ ) . وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ) فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٩٩٩/٢ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي ) ١٥ قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبركان»، و والإمام شيخنا أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه ، وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه أبي عبد الله الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
The noble Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani: he (Sanusi) took from him the seven Quranic readings. And Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isa al-Maghili, known as al-Jallab: he took from him jurisprudence. And the upright scholar Abu Abdullah al-Habbak: he took from him the science of the astrolabe. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani: he read with him usul (principles of jurisprudence), logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence. And the memorizer Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother: he read with him the 'Risala' (of Ibn Abi Zayd?), and he and his brother read with the pious Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid (theology). And he occupied himself with transmission and the sciences of athar (hadith) under the pious Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, so he narrated from him the 'Sahihayn' (the two Sahihs) and other hadith and athar books, and he (al-Tha'alibi) granted him ijaza (authorization) for what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat (chains of transmission with a special feature) and other things. And he read inheritance law and calculation under the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him ijaza for everything he narrates, and also Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif granted him ijaza on the authority of his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. (1) The scholar Muhammad Makhluq mentioned that in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fahras al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: 'He had a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of primacy, the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, the handshake, the interlacing of fingers, wearing the patchwork cloak, giving the prayer beads, and the instillation of dhikr via his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.' 15. The scholar al-Balawi said: 'And he (Sanusi) took from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah, the righteous Imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan'; and our shaykh Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him; and others. And he also took from Ibn Marzuq, our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the jurist Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the great jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar'; I think he took from him. And he took the science of calculation and inheritance from the eminent jurist in these two fields Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his aforementioned brother. And from these are those whom his student, our companion, the great accomplished blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali, included in the book 'al-Ta'rif bihi' (the introduction to him).'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account listing the teachers from whom Imam al-Sanusi studied various Islamic sciences and the authorizations he received. It begins by naming the first teacher, Abu al-Hajjaj, from whom he learned the seven Quranic readings. Then it mentions Shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Maghili for fiqh, Abu Abdullah al-Habbak for the astrolabe, and Imam al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh. Next, his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti taught him the 'Risala' (likely of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani), and both brothers read with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi the 'Irshad' of al-Juwayni and theology. The passage then describes his engagement with hadith transmission under Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and other works, and received ijaza (authorization to teach and transmit). He also studied inheritance and accounting with Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who granted him ijaza, as did Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif. After that comes a footnote from the editor (Muhammad Makhluq and al-Kattani) providing additional information on Sanusi's general ijaza from al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and mentioning a small register of hadith chains. Finally, the passage cites al-Balawi, who adds more teachers: Abu Ali al-Ahsan ('Abarkan'), Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Jallab, al-Gharabili, and Ibn Tumart for calculation and inheritance. The passage ends by noting that these teachers were collected by his student al-Mallali in a biography. The overall structure is a cumulative list, with the author's main text followed by a footnote and a quotation, all serving to establish Sanusi's credentials and the breadth of his education.

Sufi Influence on Sanusi: Ibrahim al-Tazi
Single spiritual influence identified and described.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Sufi influence on Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual development and the qualities that made Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi his primary mentor.

Core Idea
Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi was the greatest spiritual influence on Sanusi.

Imam al-Sanusi was shaped by many scholars, but one figure stands out in his spiritual formation. This passage introduces Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi, a scholar and saint who combined deep learning with the refined manners of the spiritual elite. Let's explore why he is singled out as the primary influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once aloud if possible. Notice the flow: general statement, then specific focus on al-Tazi, then listing his attributes, and finally a quote praising him.
The structure moves from general to specific.
2
Identify al-Tazi's qualifications
The passage lists several scholarly and spiritual qualities. List them: imamate in Quranic sciences, linguistics, hadith memorization, fiqh and usul, sharp insight, and the manners of saints.
These show he was both a scholar and a saint.
3
Understand the supporting quote
The author quotes al-Tinbukti to reinforce al-Tazi's majesty. The proverb about his intellect and forbearance indicates his high reputation.
This external testimony strengthens the claim.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why identifying a primary spiritual mentor is important for understanding Sanusi's own teachings. It connects his intellectual and spiritual lineage.
Sanusi's later work integrated both.

تصوف وتربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من الجانب ؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان ، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه . . كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في «نيل الابتهاج » عن ابن صعد صاحب « النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من جلالته وسعادته : أنَّ المثل ضرب بعقله وحلمه ، واشتهر في الآفاق
Sufism and his moral upbringing: There are major gnostic figures who influenced Imam al-Sanusi, but what appears is that the saintly righteous gnostic shaykh Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran, was the one with the greatest impact on Imam al-Sanusi from this aspect; for besides his imamate in the sciences of the Qur'an and the science of language, his memorization of hadith, and his vast knowledge of jurisprudence and its principles, and his sharpness of insight and understanding, he was endowed with the manners of the saints and the perfect ones. The scholar al-Tinbukti transmitted in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' from Ibn Sa'd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thaqib': 'Sufficient for you of his majesty and blessedness is that proverbs were coined about his intellect and forbearance, and he became famous in all regions.'
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the spiritual and ethical (Sufi) influences on Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by stating that there were many gnostic figures who influenced him, but then it singles out Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi as having the greatest impact. The passage lists al-Tazi's qualifications: his mastery of Quranic sciences, linguistics, hadith memorization, deep knowledge of fiqh and its principles, and sharp insight. It then adds that he possessed the manners (ādāb) of the saints and perfect ones. The author supports this by quoting al-Tinbukti's 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj', which in turn quotes Ibn Sa'd praising al-Tazi's intellect and forbearance to the point that proverbial expressions were made about them, and his fame spread far. The passage thus serves to establish al-Tazi's stature and his role as the primary spiritual mentor of Sanusi.

Sanusi's Teachers and Scholarly Education
List of Sanusi's teachers from al-Alawi's account

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize the breadth of Sanusi's traditional education through his diverse teachers in various Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Sanusi learned from multiple scholars, mastering fiqh, arithmetic, and hadith.

This passage from al-Alawi lists the teachers from whom Sanusi studied in his hometown and beyond. It demonstrates the comprehensive Islamic education that formed the foundation of his later scholarly work. Notice the variety: from jurists to mathematicians to Sufi masters, each contributing to his intellectual formation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to understand the flow of names and descriptions.
Notice the pattern: 'Akhadha min...'.
2
Identify each teacher mentioned
List the teachers: Abu Ali al-Ahsan, Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Furu'i, al-Jallab, al-Gharabili, Abu Abdullah ibn Tumarat, and his brother. Note their specialties where given.
Some are described as 'imam', 'faqih', etc.
3
Notice the range of sciences
The passage mentions arithmetic, inheritance law (fara'id), and fiqh. This shows Sanusi studied both transmitted and rational sciences.
This diversity was typical of great scholars.
4
Consider the role of his disciple
The passage ends by noting that his disciple Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali compiled these teachers in his book. Why is this important for historical transmission?
It shows the care of students in preserving their teacher's legacy.

قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبركان»، والإمام شيخنا أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه ، وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه أبي عبد الله الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
تصوف و تربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من الجانب ؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان ، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه . . كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في «نيل الابتهاج » عن ابن صعد صاحب « النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من جلالته وسعادته : أنَّ المثل ضرب بعقله وحلمه ، واشتهر في الآفاق ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن ؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال : كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي ، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال : لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا ؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق ، والصبر على المكاره ، واصطناع المعروف للناس ، والمداراة ، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه ، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته ، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة ، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة ؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة ، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار ((۱)
6وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي : صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل وانتسابه له ، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام ؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي ، والحافظ التنسي ، والإمام أحمد زروق
•
قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في « البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » : ( أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران ؛ ألبسه الخرقة ، وحدَّثه بها عن شيوخه ، وبصق في فيه ، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة ((۲)
والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي ، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي
(۱) انظر ( نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٦٠ ) ، وذكر أنه توفي سنة ( ٨٦٦هـ ) ، وإليه تنسب الطريقة التازية .
(۲) البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان ( ص ۲۳۸ )
Al-Alawi said: 'He studied with the scholars of his town, from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah the Exalted, the imam, the scholar, the righteous, Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as Abarkan, and the imam, our shaykh, Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not study much with him, and others. He also studied with Ibn Marzuq, our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the faqih Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the noble faqih Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of the versification of al-Mukhtasar, I think he studied with him. He studied the sciences of arithmetic and inheritance division with the faqih distinguished in them, Abu Abdullah ibn Tumarat, and also studied with his aforementioned brother, and from those whom his disciple, our companion the noble faqih, the accomplished, the blessed Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in his book al-Ta'rif bihi.'
His Sufism and moral upbringing: There were great spiritual figures who influenced Imam al-Sanusi, but what appears is that the shaykh, the saint, the knower, the righteous Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, the resident of Oran, had the greatest influence on Imam al-Sanusi from the spiritual side. For, in addition to his imamate in the sciences of the Quran and linguistics, preservation of hadith, breadth of his knowledge of fiqh and its principles, and sharpness of his insight and understanding, he was adorned with the manners of the saints and the perfect ones. Al-Tanbakti in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' narrated from Ibn Sa'd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thaqib': 'Sufficient for you of his majesty and felicity is that he was proverbial for his intellect and forbearance, and his fame for virtue and knowledge spread in the horizons until now. If someone exaggerated in describing a man, he would say: He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi. And if one of them became filled with rage, he would say: If I were in the position of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have endured this, because of what he used to endure of people's harm, patience in adversity, doing good to people, and amicable behavior. So he is one whom Allah manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller for the dissemination of his miracles, enwrapped with the robe of love and awe, with the acceptance he had in the hearts of the elite and common people. He called them to Allah with insight, and guided them to His servitude with the creeds of tawhid and the litanies of dhikr.'
One of the blessings of Imam al-Sanusi was his companionship with this noble knower and his affiliation to him. And distinguished figures shared this with him, such as his maternal brother Shaykh Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq.
The historian scholar Ibn Maryam al-Maliti said in 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-Ulama' bi Tilmisan': 'He studied with the imam, the scholar, the saint, the ascetic, the sincere counselor, Ibrahim al-Tazi, the resident of Oran; he clothed him with the khirqa, and narrated it to him from his shaykhs, and spat in his mouth, and narrated many things from him.'
Al-Tazi al-Arif put on the khirqa according to the method of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and put it on from Shaykh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi.
(1) See 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' (p. 60), and it mentions that he died in the year 866 AH, and the Tazi order is attributed to him.
(2) 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-Ulama' bi Tilmisan' (p. 238).
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from a commentary on Sanusi. It begins by quoting al-Alawi, who lists Sanusi's teachers. These include: from his hometown: the saint Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as Abarkan, and the imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas (though he did not study much with him), and others. He also studied with Ibn Marzuq, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the faqih Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i al-Jallab, and Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili (author of a versification of al-Mukhtasar). He studied arithmetic and inheritance law with Abu Abdullah ibn Tumarat, and also with his brother. These teachers were recorded by his disciple Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali in his book 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.

Next, the passage discusses Sanusi's spiritual formation: 'His Sufism and moral upbringing.' It states that although many spiritual figures influenced him, the greatest impact came from Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Tazi, a resident of Oran. Al-Tazi was a master in Quranic sciences, linguistics, hadith, fiqh and its principles, and had sharp insight. He was distinguished by his manners and virtues. The passage quotes al-Tanbakti, who quotes Ibn Sa'd, describing how people used al-Tazi as a proverbial example of intellect and forbearance. It gives examples: if someone praised a man, they would compare him to al-Tazi; if angry, they would say they could not endure as al-Tazi did, because he endured people's harm, practiced patience, did good, and was amicable. Al-Tazi was a guide for creation, calling to Allah with insight, and teaching tawhid and dhikr.

Then the passage notes that Sanusi's companionship with al-Tazi was a great blessing. Other notable figures also shared this relationship: his maternal brother Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq.

Ibn Maryam al-Maliti's 'al-Bustan' is quoted, describing how al-Tazi clothed Sanusi with the khirqa (Sufi cloak), narrated it from his shaykhs, spat in his mouth (a traditional blessing), and narrated many things to him.

Finally, the passage traces the chain of the khirqa: al-Tazi received it from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, who received it from Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi.

The footnotes specify that al-Tazi died in 866 AH and that the Tazi order is named after him, and provide the source for the al-Bustan quote.

The Spiritual Influence of Ibrahim al-Tazi
Account of Ibrahim al-Tazi's influence and the khirqa transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound spiritual impact of Ibrahim al-Tazi on Imam al-Sanusi and the significance of the khirqa transmission.

Core Idea
Ibrahim al-Tazi was the greatest spiritual influence on Sanusi, exemplifying patience, wisdom, and sainthood.

After listing his many teachers, the biography turns to Sanusi's spiritual formation, highlighting the decisive role of the Sufi master Ibrahim al-Tazi. This passage describes al-Tazi's virtues, his reputation, and the formal transmission of the Sufi cloak (khirqa) to Sanusi. It reveals how spiritual mentorship was as crucial as academic learning in shaping Sanusi's path.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Tazi
Read the Arabic and translation describing al-Tazi's character and influence.
Notice the vivid language: 'proverbial for intellect and forbearance'.
2
Note the specific virtues of al-Tazi
The passage mentions his patience, enduring harm, doing good, and his role as a guide. How do these traits reflect the Sufi ideal?
He is described as a 'caller for the dissemination of his miracles'.
3
Understand the khirqa transmission
The passage explains that al-Tazi clothed Sanusi with the khirqa, a symbol of spiritual authorization. Identify the chain: al-Tazi from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i from Salih al-Zawawi.
This chain links Sanusi to earlier Sufi masters.
4
Consider the broader context
The passage also names other students of al-Tazi, like Ali al-Taluti and Ahmad Zarruq. What does this tell us about al-Tazi's role in the scholarly community?
He was a major spiritual influence in the region.

قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبركان»، والإمام شيخنا أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه ، وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه أبي عبد الله الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، ( وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
تصوف و تربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من الجانب ؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان ، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه . . كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في «نيل الابتهاج » عن ابن صعد صاحب « النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من جلالته وسعادته : أنَّ المثل ضرب بعقله وحلمه ، واشتهر في الآفاق ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن ؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال : كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي ، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال : لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا ؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق ، والصبر على المكاره ، واصطناع المعروف للناس ، والمداراة ، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه ، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته ، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة ، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة ؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة ، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار ((۱)
6وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي : صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل وانتسابه له ، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام ؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي ، والحافظ التنسي ، والإمام أحمد زروق

قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في « البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » : ( أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران ؛ ألبسه الخرقة ، وحدَّثه بها عن شيوخه ، وبصق في فيه ، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة ((۲)
والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي ، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي
(۱) انظر ( نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٦٠ ) ، وذكر أنه توفي سنة ( ٨٦٦هـ ) ، وإليه تنسب الطريقة التازية .
(۲) البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان ( ص ۲۳۸ )
Al-Alawi said: 'He studied with the scholars of his town, from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah the Exalted, the imam, the scholar, the righteous, Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as Abarkan, and the imam, our shaykh, Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not study much with him, and others. He also studied with Ibn Marzuq, our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the faqih Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the noble faqih Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of the versification of al-Mukhtasar, I think he studied with him. He studied the sciences of arithmetic and inheritance division with the faqih distinguished in them, Abu Abdullah ibn Tumarat, and also studied with his aforementioned brother, and from those whom his disciple, our companion the noble faqih, the accomplished, the blessed Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in his book al-Ta'rif bihi.'
His Sufism and moral upbringing: There were great spiritual figures who influenced Imam al-Sanusi, but what appears is that the shaykh, the saint, the knower, the righteous Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, the resident of Oran, had the greatest influence on Imam al-Sanusi from the spiritual side. For, in addition to his imamate in the sciences of the Quran and linguistics, preservation of hadith, breadth of his knowledge of fiqh and its principles, and sharpness of his insight and understanding, he was adorned with the manners of the saints and the perfect ones. Al-Tanbakti in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' narrated from Ibn Sa'd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thaqib': 'Sufficient for you of his majesty and felicity is that he was proverbial for his intellect and forbearance, and his fame for virtue and knowledge spread in the horizons until now. If someone exaggerated in describing a man, he would say: He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi. And if one of them became filled with rage, he would say: If I were in the position of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have endured this, because of what he used to endure of people's harm, patience in adversity, doing good to people, and amicable behavior. So he is one whom Allah manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller for the dissemination of his miracles, enwrapped with the robe of love and awe, with the acceptance he had in the hearts of the elite and common people. He called them to Allah with insight, and guided them to His servitude with the creeds of tawhid and the litanies of dhikr.'
One of the blessings of Imam al-Sanusi was his companionship with this noble knower and his affiliation to him. And distinguished figures shared this with him, such as his maternal brother Shaykh Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq.
The historian scholar Ibn Maryam al-Maliti said in 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-Ulama' bi Tilmisan': 'He studied with the imam, the scholar, the saint, the ascetic, the sincere counselor, Ibrahim al-Tazi, the resident of Oran; he clothed him with the khirqa, and narrated it to him from his shaykhs, and spat in his mouth, and narrated many things from him.'
Al-Tazi al-Arif put on the khirqa according to the method of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and put it on from Shaykh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi.
(1) See 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' (p. 60), and it mentions that he died in the year 866 AH, and the Tazi order is attributed to him.
(2) 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-Ulama' bi Tilmisan' (p. 238).
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from a commentary on Sanusi. It begins by quoting al-Alawi, who lists Sanusi's teachers. These include: from his hometown: the saint Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as Abarkan, and the imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas (though he did not study much with him), and others. He also studied with Ibn Marzuq, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the faqih Abu Abdullah al-Furu'i al-Jallab, and Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili (author of a versification of al-Mukhtasar). He studied arithmetic and inheritance law with Abu Abdullah ibn Tumarat, and also with his brother. These teachers were recorded by his disciple Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali in his book 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.

Next, the passage discusses Sanusi's spiritual formation: 'His Sufism and moral upbringing.' It states that although many spiritual figures influenced him, the greatest impact came from Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Tazi, a resident of Oran. Al-Tazi was a master in Quranic sciences, linguistics, hadith, fiqh and its principles, and had sharp insight. He was distinguished by his manners and virtues. The passage quotes al-Tanbakti, who quotes Ibn Sa'd, describing how people used al-Tazi as a proverbial example of intellect and forbearance. It gives examples: if someone praised a man, they would compare him to al-Tazi; if angry, they would say they could not endure as al-Tazi did, because he endured people's harm, practiced patience, did good, and was amicable. Al-Tazi was a guide for creation, calling to Allah with insight, and teaching tawhid and dhikr.

Then the passage notes that Sanusi's companionship with al-Tazi was a great blessing. Other notable figures also shared this relationship: his maternal brother Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq.

Ibn Maryam al-Maliti's 'al-Bustan' is quoted, describing how al-Tazi clothed Sanusi with the khirqa (Sufi cloak), narrated it from his shaykhs, spat in his mouth (a traditional blessing), and narrated many things to him.

Finally, the passage traces the chain of the khirqa: al-Tazi received it from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, who received it from Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi.

The footnotes specify that al-Tazi died in 866 AH and that the Tazi order is named after him, and provide the source for the al-Bustan quote.

Sanusi's Initiation with Ibrahim al-Tazi
Sanusi's connection to Ibrahim al-Tazi and Sufi initiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Sanusi received Sufi initiation from Ibrahim al-Tazi and the significance of the khirqa.

Core Idea
Sanusi's spiritual authority was rooted in a living chain of saintly transmission.

This passage introduces one of Sanusi's most influential spiritual teachers, Ibrahim al-Tazi, whose reputation for patience and wisdom was legendary. The biographical snippet highlights how al-Tazi initiated Sanusi into the Sufi path through the traditional bestowal of the khirqa (cloak), linking him to a distinguished chain of masters extending back to Abu Madyan.

Guided Path
1
Read about Ibrahim al-Tazi's virtues
Notice how al-Tazi is described as a model of patience, endurance, and diplomacy, and how people used his name as a benchmark for character.
2
Examine the initiation details
The historian Ibn Maryam reports that al-Tazi clothed Sanusi in the khirqa, narrated it from his shaykhs, and performed the symbolic spitting. Understand the significance of each action.
The khirqa represents spiritual transmission and blessing.
3
Trace the chain of transmission
Note that al-Tazi received the khirqa from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, who got it from al-Zawawi, who got it from Abu Madyan. This chain shows the authenticity of Sanusi's spiritual lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال: كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال: لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق، والصبر على المكاره، واصطناع المعروف للناس، والمداراة، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار. وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي: صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل وانتسابه له، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي، والحافظ التنسي، والإمام أحمد زروق. قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في «البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان»: (أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران؛ ألبسه الخرقة، وحدَّثه بها عن شيوخه، وبصق في فيه، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة). والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير. ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها.. الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي الراشدي، شهر بأبركان، ومعناه بلسان البربرية: الأسود، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به، وكان يقول: (رأيت المشايخ والأولياء، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان). وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي، وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له: (جعلك الله الأئمة من المتقين)، قال العلامة ابن مريم: (فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته فيه تبسم له). وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد.. وضع يديه على رأسه وقال: نقرة خالصة! ويظهر أنَّ محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه: (من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن).
His virtue and knowledge were mentioned until now; if someone exaggerates in describing a man, he says: 'He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi.' And if one of them becomes filled with rage, he says: 'If I were in the position of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have endured this!' because of what he used to endure from the harm of people, patience in hardships, doing good to people, and diplomacy. So he is one whom God manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller to spread His miracles, cloaked in the garment of love and awe, along with what he has of acceptance in the hearts of the elite and commoners. So he called them to God with insight, and guided them to His servitude through the creeds of tawhid (monotheism) and the functions of dhikr (remembrance). And it was part of the blessing of Imam al-Sanusi: his companionship with this noble mystic and his affiliation with him. And renowned figures shared this with him, such as his maternal brother Sheikh 'Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq. The scholar historian Ibn Maryam al-Maliti said in 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-'Ulama' bi Tilimsan': 'He learned from the Imam, the scholar, the saint, the ascetic, the advisor, Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Wahran; he clothed him in the khirqa (Sufi cloak), narrated it to him from his shaykhs, spat into his mouth, and narrated many things from him.' And the mystic al-Tazi had worn the khirqa according to the way of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and he wore it from Sheikh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi with his chain to Abu Madyan, the famous mystic and great pole. And among the noble souls whose breaths contacted our Imam al-Sanusi: the imam, the jurist, the great pole, al-Hasan ibn Makhluf ibn Mas'ud al-Mazili al-Rashidi, known as Abrkan, which in the Berber language means 'the black one'. He accompanied him much and benefited from him. He used to say: 'I have seen the shaykhs and the saints, and I have not seen anyone like my master al-Hasan Abrkan.' And when Imam al-Sanusi entered upon him and opened the conversation, he said to him: 'May God make you among the imams of the pious.' The scholar Ibn Maryam said: 'God verified his discernment and prayer in him; he smiled at him.' And in his childhood, when he passed with the boys by Imam Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, he placed his hands on his head and said: 'A pure gold nugget!' And it appears that the love of the Sufis had imprinted his heart, so he strived earnestly for leadership in their path, and it is not a path of 'say it' but of seriousness, perseverance, and action, and therefore you find the complaint of folding its carpet, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the marvels in our time is that there exists a scholar who has been gathered for him the knowledge of the outward and the inward.'
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual teachers and early formation. It begins by praising the virtues of Sidi Ibrahim al-Tazi, describing his reputation for patience and kindness, and presents him as a man of great spiritual stature. It then notes that al-Sanusi was blessed to be his companion and affiliate. Several other scholars shared this connection. The historian Ibn Maryam quotes that al-Tazi initiated al-Sanusi into the Sufi order by clothing him with the khirqa (Sufi cloak), narrating traditions from his own shaykhs, and performing the symbolic act of spitting into his mouth—a traditional means of transmitting spiritual blessings. The chain of this khirqa is traced back to Abu Madyan, a renowned saint and 'pole' of Sufism. The passage then turns to another teacher, al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrkan (meaning 'black one' in Berber). Al-Sanusi benefited greatly from him and considered him unique among the saints. Ibn Maryam confirms the efficacy of al-Mazili's prayer for al-Sanusi. A childhood anecdote is mentioned: when al-Sanusi passed by the scholar Ibn Marzuq as a boy, Ibn Marzuq predicted his future greatness by calling him 'a pure gold nugget.' The passage concludes with al-Sanusi's own remark on the rarity of a scholar combining outward (exoteric) and inward (esoteric) sciences, reflecting the ideal of integrating formal learning with spiritual realization.

إبراهيم التازي
الخرقة
أبو مدين

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Sanusi was only a scholar of formal theology, but this passage shows he was deeply rooted in Sufi initiation and practice.
Correction: Sanusi's spiritual formation included initiatic transmission (khirqa) from a saintly teacher, connecting him to a lineage of Sufi masters.

C) Recited a prayer over him

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's initiation by al-Tazi connected him to a prophetic chain of spiritual transmission through the khirqa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The people of Tlemcen would praise al-Tazi's patience to the point of saying they could not endure what he endured. Think of a recent situation where you felt anger or frustration. How does al-Tazi’s example challenge you to respond differently? What specific step will you take this week to practice patience when you feel justified in being upset?
?
Sanusi was initiated into a spiritual chain reaching back to Abu Madyan. You too are connected to the Prophet through scholars and saints. When you recite the shahada or make dhikr, do you feel that connection? What would change in your daily practice if you truly lived as part of this living chain?
?
Al-Tazi guided people through the creeds of tawhid and the functions of dhikr. Are you balancing sound belief with consistent spiritual practice? If not, which side needs more attention? Make a concrete plan to integrate both more deeply into your routine starting tomorrow.

Sanusi's Teacher al-Hasan al-Mazili and His Early Promise
Sanusi's relationship with al-Hasan al-Mazili and early prophecy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn about Sanusi's second teacher, al-Hasan al-Mazili, and the childhood prediction by Ibn Marzuq that marked his destiny.

Core Idea
Even as a child, Sanusi was recognized as a 'pure gold nugget' of spiritual potential.

The passage continues with another key figure in Sanusi's spiritual formation: al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrkan. Sanusi held him in the highest esteem. The narrative also includes a charming childhood anecdote where the scholar Ibn Marzuq predicted Sanusi's future greatness, and ends with Sanusi's own reflection on the rarity of combining outward and inward knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Hasan al-Mazili
Notice Sanusi's high praise for al-Mazili, calling him unique among saints, and the account of Ibn Maryam confirming the effectiveness of al-Mazili's prayer.
The name 'Abrkan' means 'the black one' in Berber.
2
Understand the childhood prediction
When passing by Ibn Marzuq as a child, he placed his hands on Sanusi's head and called him 'a pure gold nugget' – a prophecy of his future spiritual eminence.
This shows early recognition of Sanusi's potential.
3
Reflect on Sanusi's concluding remark
Sanusi comments on the rarity of a scholar combining both outward (exoteric) and inward (esoteric) sciences, which he himself embodied.
This underscores the integration of formal learning and spiritual practice.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال: كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال: لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق، والصبر على المكاره، واصطناع المعروف للناس، والمداراة، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار. وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي: صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل وانتسابه له، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي، والحافظ التنسي، والإمام أحمد زروق. قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في «البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان»: (أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران؛ ألبسه الخرقة، وحدَّثه بها عن شيوخه، وبصق في فيه، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة). والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير. ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها.. الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي الراشدي، شهر بأبركان، ومعناه بلسان البربرية: الأسود، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به، وكان يقول: (رأيت المشايخ والأولياء، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان). وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي، وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له: (جعلك الله الأئمة من المتقين)، قال العلامة ابن مريم: (فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته فيه تبسم له). وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد.. وضع يديه على رأسه وقال: نقرة خالصة! ويظهر أنَّ محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه: (من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن).
His virtue and knowledge were mentioned until now; if someone exaggerates in describing a man, he says: 'He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi.' And if one of them becomes filled with rage, he says: 'If I were in the position of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have endured this!' because of what he used to endure from the harm of people, patience in hardships, doing good to people, and diplomacy. So he is one whom God manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller to spread His miracles, cloaked in the garment of love and awe, along with what he has of acceptance in the hearts of the elite and commoners. So he called them to God with insight, and guided them to His servitude through the creeds of tawhid (monotheism) and the functions of dhikr (remembrance). And it was part of the blessing of Imam al-Sanusi: his companionship with this noble mystic and his affiliation with him. And renowned figures shared this with him, such as his maternal brother Sheikh 'Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq. The scholar historian Ibn Maryam al-Maliti said in 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-'Ulama' bi Tilimsan': 'He learned from the Imam, the scholar, the saint, the ascetic, the advisor, Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Wahran; he clothed him in the khirqa (Sufi cloak), narrated it to him from his shaykhs, spat into his mouth, and narrated many things from him.' And the mystic al-Tazi had worn the khirqa according to the way of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and he wore it from Sheikh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi with his chain to Abu Madyan, the famous mystic and great pole. And among the noble souls whose breaths contacted our Imam al-Sanusi: the imam, the jurist, the great pole, al-Hasan ibn Makhluf ibn Mas'ud al-Mazili al-Rashidi, known as Abrkan, which in the Berber language means 'the black one'. He accompanied him much and benefited from him. He used to say: 'I have seen the shaykhs and the saints, and I have not seen anyone like my master al-Hasan Abrkan.' And when Imam al-Sanusi entered upon him and opened the conversation, he said to him: 'May God make you among the imams of the pious.' The scholar Ibn Maryam said: 'God verified his discernment and prayer in him; he smiled at him.' And in his childhood, when he passed with the boys by Imam Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, he placed his hands on his head and said: 'A pure gold nugget!' And it appears that the love of the Sufis had imprinted his heart, so he strived earnestly for leadership in their path, and it is not a path of 'say it' but of seriousness, perseverance, and action, and therefore you find the complaint of folding its carpet, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the marvels in our time is that there exists a scholar who has been gathered for him the knowledge of the outward and the inward.'
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual teachers and early formation. It begins by praising the virtues of Sidi Ibrahim al-Tazi, describing his reputation for patience and kindness, and presents him as a man of great spiritual stature. It then notes that al-Sanusi was blessed to be his companion and affiliate. Several other scholars shared this connection. The historian Ibn Maryam quotes that al-Tazi initiated al-Sanusi into the Sufi order by clothing him with the khirqa (Sufi cloak), narrating traditions from his own shaykhs, and performing the symbolic act of spitting into his mouth—a traditional means of transmitting spiritual blessings. The chain of this khirqa is traced back to Abu Madyan, a renowned saint and 'pole' of Sufism. The passage then turns to another teacher, al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrkan (meaning 'black one' in Berber). Al-Sanusi benefited greatly from him and considered him unique among the saints. Ibn Maryam confirms the efficacy of al-Mazili's prayer for al-Sanusi. A childhood anecdote is mentioned: when al-Sanusi passed by the scholar Ibn Marzuq as a boy, Ibn Marzuq predicted his future greatness by calling him 'a pure gold nugget.' The passage concludes with al-Sanusi's own remark on the rarity of a scholar combining outward (exoteric) and inward (esoteric) sciences, reflecting the ideal of integrating formal learning with spiritual realization.

ابن مرزوق الحفيد
علم الظاهر والباطن

Sanusi's Spiritual Lineage: Connection with Hasan al-Mazili
Describes Sanusi's relationship with his teacher Hasan al-Mazili and a childhood anecdote.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of Sanusi's connection with his teacher Hasan al-Mazili and a childhood sign of his spiritual purity.

Core Idea
Sanusi's teacher praised him as a 'pure silver piece,' foretelling his future sainthood.

This lesson introduces one of Sanusi's key teachers, Hasan al-Mazili, known as Abrakan. It shows how Sanusi benefited from him and how even as a child, scholars recognized his spiritual potential. The passage also ties Sanusi's chain to the great master Abu Madyan.

Guided Path
1

Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.

By his chain of transmission to Abu Madyan, the famous gnostic and the great pole. Sanusi's Self-Praise: The Rarest Scholar of Exoteric and Esoteric Sciences
Sanusi praises a rare scholar of exoteric and esoteric knowledge, with a student's comment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi described the rare scholar who combines zahir and batin sciences, and how his student interpreted this as a reference to Sanusi himself.

Core Idea
Sanusi's praise of a scholar may actually be a humble self-reference.

This passage offers a glimpse into Sanusi's own view of his scholarly stature. He describes a scholar of exceptional rarity—one who has mastered both outward and inward knowledge. His student al-Mallali later reveals that Sanusi was likely speaking of himself. This lesson explores the text and its subtle self-reference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the English translation. Note the poetic language used to describe the scholar.
Pay attention to the phrase 'من الغرائب' indicating rarity.
2
Analyze Sanusi's description
List the qualities of the scholar: complete mastery of zahir and batin, benefit in both sciences, extreme rarity, treasure in both worlds, need to hold fast to him.
Consider the urgency of 'فليشدَّ عليه يده' (hold fast to him).
3
Understand al-Mallali's interpretation
Read al-Mallali's comment and understand why he thinks Sanusi was referring to himself. Consider the implication that Sanusi died soon after.
Al-Mallali says 'وكأنه أشار به لنفسه' (as if he pointed to himself).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويظهر أنَّ محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه: ( من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن على أكمل وجه؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى، فليشدَّ عليه يده؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً ). عقب على هذه الكلمة الشيخ الملالي تلميذ الإمام: ( وكأنه أشار به لنفسه، فلم يلبث بعده حتى خطف، فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك، ولا شك أنه لا يوجد مثله أبداً )
And it appears that the love of the Sufis had devoured his heart, so he strove diligently to take the lead in their path, and it is not a path of speech, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action. Therefore you find complaint spreading its carpet, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the wonders in this time of ours is that there exists a scholar for whom both the science of the outward and the inward have been gathered to the most complete degree, so that benefit is derived from him in both sciences. His existence is extremely rare, so whoever finds him has found a great treasure in this world and the next. He should hold fast to him, so that he does not lose him soon and never find his like in the East or West ever again.' Al-Shaykh al-Mallali, the student of the Imam, commented on these words: 'It is as if he was pointing to himself, for he did not stay long after that until he was taken away, as if he was revealing that to us, and there is no doubt that no one like him exists ever.'
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage shows Sanusi's admiration for a scholar who has mastered both exoteric (zahir) and esoteric (batin) sciences. The context suggests Sanusi himself is that scholar. The passage begins by explaining that the love of Sufism consumed Sanusi's heart, driving him to seek leadership in the Sufi path, which is a path of action, not mere talk. Then Sanusi is quoted describing the rarity of such a scholar. He warns to hold onto such a person because his loss is permanent. Al-Mallali comments that Sanusi was referring to himself, as he died shortly after saying this.

علم الباطن
الملالي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Sanusi was referring to a known scholar like Hasan al-Mazili or Ibn Marzuq.
Correction: Al-Mallali's commentary clarifies that Sanusi was pointing to himself, as he died soon after and no one like him existed.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Who First Brought Kalam to the Maghreb? Al-Ayli's Role
Al-Shafshawni lists shared teachers and credits al-Ayli with introducing kalam to the Maghreb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Ayli is credited with introducing the science of kalam to the Maghreb in later times, and you will become familiar with the shared teachers of Sanusi and Ibn Zakri.

Core Idea
Al-Ayli was the first to bring kalam to the Maghreb.

This passage from al-Shafshawni reveals a key fact about the history of kalam in the Maghreb: it was al-Ayli, not Sanusi himself, who first introduced the discipline there. By examining the list of shared teachers between Sanusi and Ibn Zakri, we learn about the scholarly network that shaped Sanusi's education. Let's explore these names and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key claim
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that al-Shafshawni states al-Ayli was the first to introduce kalam to the Maghreb.
2
Focus on al-Ayli's title
The passage gives a detailed pronunciation guide for al-Ayli's name. This reflects the scholarly precision of the time.
The pronunciation is given: sukun on lam, fatha on hamza, etc.
3
List the other teachers
Scan the list of other teachers: Ibn Marzuq, Ibn al-Abbas, etc. Note that they are all described as commentators or scholars.
These names link Sanusi to a wide scholarly tradition.
4
Consider the students of these teachers
The second part from al-Tanbakti lists notable students who studied under these teachers, including Ibn Sa'd and al-Zawawi.
5
Reflect on the historical significance
Think about why it matters who introduced kalam to the Maghreb. This shows how knowledge spread through traveling scholars.
Al-Ayli is called 'al-rahhal' (the traveler).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال العلامة الشفشاوني: ( وأشياخه وأشياخ ابن زكري واحد، ومن أشياخهما العالم الرحال الأيلي، بسكون اللام وفتح الهمزة وضم الياء وكسر اللام، وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة، والشيخ ابن مرزوق شارح « البردة »، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن العباس شارح « لامية ابن مالك »، والشيخ أبو العباس أحمد بن زاغ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله أقرقار، والشيخ أبو عثمان قاسم العقباني، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن الجلاب، أفادني بذلك شيخنا أبو عبد الله محمد شقرون بن هبة الله. قال العلامة التنبكتي: ( أخذ عنه أعلام؛ كابن صعد، وأبي القاسم الزواوي، وابن أبي مدين، والشيخ يحيى بن محمد )
And the scholar al-Shafshawni said: 'His teachers and the teachers of Ibn Zakri are the same. Among their teachers is the traveler scholar al-Ayli, with sukun of the lam, fatha of the hamza, damm of the ya, and kasr of the lam. He is the first to introduce the science of kalam into the Maghreb in later times. And Shaykh Ibn Marzuq, the commentator of al-Burda, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas, the commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik, and Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zaghu, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Aqraqar, and Shaykh Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Jallab. My teacher Abu Abd Allah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah informed me of that.' The scholar al-Tanbakti said: 'Eminent figures studied under him, such as Ibn Sa'd, Abu al-Qasim al-Zawawi, Ibn Abi Madyan, and Shaykh Yahya ibn Muhammad.'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage provides a list of teachers shared between Imam al-Sanusi and Ibn Zakri, emphasizing the scholarly lineage. It highlights al-Ayli as the one who first introduced 'ilm al-kalam into the Maghreb in later times, which is a significant point for the history of this science. The passage then lists several other teachers, including Ibn Marzuq and others, and ends with a list of students who studied under one of these figures.

المغرب
الأيلي
الشفشاوني
التنبكتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Imam al-Sanusi himself introduced kalam to the Maghreb.
Correction: The text clearly states that al-Ayli, not Sanusi, was the first to introduce kalam to the Maghreb in later times.

?

The Rarity and Value of Sanusi's Work as Praised by al-Mallali
A student's comment on the rarity of Sanusi's work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a student of Sanusi expressed the exceptional value and rarity of his teacher's work and the historical context of its preservation.

Core Idea
A treasure so rare it was destined to be lost, yet its loss affirms its greatness.

This short passage gives us a glimpse into the reverence that students of Imam al-Sanusi had for his work. It is not a theological argument, but a testimony to the perceived excellence of the book. As we read, we see how al-Mallali interpreted a previous praise as a prophecy of the work's eventual rarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the original praise
Read the first part of the Arabic passage, which praises a work as extremely rare and a great treasure. Notice the phrases 'fi ghāyat al-nudūr' and 'kanzan ʿaẓīman'.
This praise likely refers to Sanusi's own work.
2
Understand the key terms
Learn the meaning of two key words: 'al-nudūr' (الندور) meaning rarity, and 'al-kanz' (الكنز) meaning treasure. These convey the high value placed on the work.
3
Read al-Mallali's comment
Read the second part where al-Mallali, a student of Sanusi, comments that the praise seemed to point to Sanusi himself, and the work was soon 'snatched away' (khuṭifa).
This gives a historical context of loss.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why such a testimonial is important: it shows the esteem in which Sanusi's work was held and the urgency of preserving scholarly works.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أكمل وجه ؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين ، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور ، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى ، فليشدَّ عليه يده ؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً ) .
عقب على هذه الكلمة الشيخ الملالي تلميذ الإمام : ( وكأنه أشار به لنفسه ، فلم يلبث بعده حتى خطف ، فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك ، ولا شك أنه لا يوجد مثله أبداً ) (۱) .
(۱) انظر ( نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٥٦٥ - ٥٦٦ )
To the most perfect degree, so that benefit is derived from it in the two sciences. So the existence of its like is extremely rare. Whoever finds it has found a great treasure, worldly and otherworldly. So let him hold fast to it, lest it be lost soon and he never find its like in East or West forever.)
Al-Mallali, the student of the Imam, commented on this statement: 'It is as if he pointed to himself, for he did not remain after it until it was snatched away, as if he revealed that to us. And there is no doubt that its like will never be found.' (1)
(1) See Nayl al-ibtihaj, pp. 565-566.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts. First, a quote praising the exceptional quality and rarity of a work (likely Sanusi's own work). The quote urges the reader to hold fast to it because it is a great treasure. Second, al-Mallali, a student of Sanusi, comments that this praise seems to refer to Sanusi himself, and shortly after, the work was 'snatched away' (perhaps meaning it became lost or rare). He affirms that nothing like it will ever be found. The passage includes a footnote reference to Nayl al-ibtihaj.

Sanusi's Teachers According to al-Shafshawani
Al-Shafshawani lists the teachers of Imam Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage of Imam Sanusi and the significance of al-Ayli in bringing the science of kalam to the Maghrib.

Core Idea
Sanusi's teachers were shared with Ibn Zakari, and al-Ayli brought kalam to the Maghrib.

This passage from al-Shafshawani provides a valuable historical record of Imam Sanusi's teachers. It highlights the key figure al-Ayli, who is credited with introducing the science of kalam (theology) to the Maghrib in later times. The list also includes other notable scholars, showing the breadth of Sanusi's education and his connection to a wider scholarly network.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the names and the brief description of al-Ayli's role.
The passage is a quotation from al-Shafshawani.
2
Identify the teachers
List the teachers mentioned. Notice that al-Shafshawani says Sanusi's teachers and Ibn Zakari's teachers are the same.
There are seven teachers listed in total.
3
Focus on al-Ayli's significance
Al-Ayli is highlighted as the first to introduce kalam to the Maghrib. Consider why this is important for the spread of Islamic theology.
4
Understand the chain of transmission
Note that al-Shafshawani credits his own teacher for the information. This shows the importance of oral transmission in Islamic scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال العلامة الشفشاوني : ( وأشياخه وأشياخ ابن زكري واحد ، ومن أشياخهما العالم الرحال الأيلي ، بسكون اللام وفتح الهمزة وضم الياء وكسر اللام ، وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة ، والشيخ ابن مرزوق شارح « البردة » ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن العباس شارح ) لامية ابن مالك » ، والشيخ أبو العباس أحمد بن زاغ ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله أقرقار ، والشيخ أبو عثمان قاسم العقباني ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن الجلاب ، أفادني بذلك شيخنا أبو عبد الله محمد شقرون بن هبة الله ((٢)
(۲) انظر ( دوحة الناشر » ( ص ١٢٢ ) .
And the scholar al-Shafshawani said: 'His teachers and the teachers of Ibn Zakari are one. Among their teachers are the traveling scholar al-Ayli — with sukun on the lam, fatha on the hamza, dhamma on the ya, and kasra on the lam — and he was the first to introduce the science of kalam to the Maghrib in later times. And Shaykh Ibn Marzuq, commentator of al-Burda; and Shaykh Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik; and Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zag; and Shaykh Abu Abdullah Aqrar; and Shaykh Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani; and Shaykh Abu Abdullah ibn al-Jallab. My teacher Abu Abdullah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah informed me of that.' (2)
(2) See Dawhat al-nashir, p. 122.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Shafshawani in which he identifies the teachers of Imam Sanusi. He begins by noting that Sanusi's teachers and the teachers of Ibn Zakari are the same. Then he lists them: first, al-Ayli, noting his name's vocalization and that he was the first to introduce kalam to the Maghrib in later times. Then he lists six more teachers: Ibn Marzuq, the commentator of al-Burda; Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik; Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zag; Abu Abdullah Aqrar; Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani; and Abu Abdullah ibn al-Jallab. He credits his own teacher, Abu Abdullah Muhammad Shaqrun, for this information. The passage ends with a footnote reference to Dawhat al-nashir.

علم الكلام

Al-Tanbakti's List of Sanusi's Eminent Students
Al-Tanbakti enumerates the notable students of Sanusi.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Sanusi's students were the leading scholars of their time.

Al-Tanbakti, a later biographer, lists the eminent students who studied under Imam al-Sanusi. This passage gives us a glimpse into the intellectual lineage and influence of Sanusi's teaching. The list includes nine named individuals, each a scholar in their own right, and refers to 'other virtuous people.'

Students of Sanusi: al-Mallali, Zarruq, and al-Balawi
Mentions of three students and their specific connections to Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different types of relationships Sanusi's students had with him, as documented by al-Mallali, Zarruq, and al-Balawi.

Core Idea
Great scholars can be students, peers, and even historians of their teachers.

This passage introduces three notable figures connected to Imam Sanusi: al-Mallali, who wrote Sanusi's biography but omitted a chapter on his students; Zarruq, a peer who explicitly studied under Sanusi; and al-Balawi, who attended general sessions. Each relationship tells us something about scholarly transmission and respect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation once without analysing. Get a feel for the names and relationships.
Notice that the passage has three distinct parts, each about a different person.
2
Identify each student and their connection
For each of the three students (al-Mallali, Zarruq, al-Balawi), note what the passage says about their relationship with Sanusi. What is unique about each?
Al-Mallali was a historian; Zarruq was a peer and stated his discipleship; al-Balawi attended sessions but didn't read directly.
3
Consider the footnote's extra information
Read the footnote about Zarruq's Egyptian teachers and Sanusi's lack of an eastern journey. How does this distinction matter?
It shows that Zarruq had a broader geographical network, yet still acknowledged Sanusi as his teacher.
4
Reflect on scholarly humility
Think about how these students, themselves great scholars, chose to document their connection to Sanusi. What does this teach about the tradition of isnad and scholarly lineage?

And al-Mallali did not dedicate a chapter to discussing those who studied under Imam Sanusi, while he himself is one of his prominent students, the historian of his life, and the collector of his reports and states.
And among those who studied under Imam Sanusi while being among his peers and the dignitaries of his time: the Imam, the gnostic of Allah, Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Barnusi al-Fasi, known as Zarruq, who died in the year 899 AH, of great standing and high rank. He shared many of his teachers with Sanusi, and he explicitly stated his study under Imam Sanusi himself, as narrated by the historian al-Tanbakti. (2)
And among the eminent people who met him and attended his general sessions without directly reading under him: Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Ali al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashi, died in 938 AH. He chronicled him and his fragrant biography in his Thabat.

Commentary
This passage consists of three parts. First, it notes that al-Mallali, though a prominent student and biographer of Sanusi, did not write a chapter about Sanusi's students. Second, it mentions Ahmad Zarruq, a renowned scholar, who studied under Sanusi despite being his contemporary and sharing many teachers. Zarruq explicitly stated he studied under Sanusi, as recorded by al-Tanbakti. Third, it mentions Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, who attended Sanusi's general sessions without formal reading. The footnote adds that Zarruq was distinguished from Sanusi by having teachers from Egypt, while Sanusi apparently did not travel to the East.

Students and Associates of Imam al-Sanusi
Lists students of Sanusi and quotes al-Balawi's description of his teaching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circle of students around Imam al-Sanusi and the vibrant teaching environment in which his 'Aqidah al-Sughra was studied.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi’s students recited his creed from memory in unison—a living tradition.

This lesson introduces us to the scholars who studied with or attended the gatherings of Imam al-Sanusi. Among the accounts, the most vivid comes from Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, who describes how al-Sanusi's 'Aqidah al-Sughra was recited by heart after Friday prayers. It offers a window into the pedagogical atmosphere of 9th-century Tlemcen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the names and events.
This is a biographical section, so focus on the flow of the narrative.
2
Identify key figures
Note the list of students, especially Zarruq and al-Balawi, and their relationship to al-Sanusi.
Zarruq is a well-known scholar who explicitly stated studying under al-Sanusi.
3
Focus on al-Balawi's description
Pay attention to the details of the teaching session: what was read, how, and the recitation of the 'Aqidah al-Sughra.
Al-Sanusi's students and commoners recited the creed by heart in unison after 'Asr on Fridays.
4
Reflect on the missed opportunity
Al-Balawi regretted not being able to read directly under al-Sanusi due to the constant occupation of the students.
This demonstrates the high demand for al-Sanusi's teaching.

ومن جملة الأعلام الذين اجتمعوا به، وحضروا عموم مجالسه دون القراءة عليه مباشرةً : أبو جعفر أحمد بن علي البلوي الوادي آشي . المتوفى سنة ( ٩٣٨هـ )، وقد أرَّخَ له ولسيرته العطرة في « ثبته »

وحرصي
وقال : ( ولم تقدَّرْ لي القراءة عليه مع رغبتي في ذلك عليه؛ لاستغراق طلبته أوقات قعوده، حتى إنهم كانوا يقرؤون عليه والرملية في يد أحدهم إذا فرغت قطع، وكنت أؤمل القراءة وأترصد لها وقتاً، فعاجلته - قدَّسَهُ الله تعالى - المَنِيَّةُ، ولم أنل من ذلك لأُمْنِيَّة ( (٢) .
(۱) انظر « ثبت أبي جعفر البلوي » ( ص ٤٣٦ ) . (۲) انظر « ثبت أبي جعفر البلوي » ( ص ٤٣٧ )
And Ibn al-Hajj al-Baydari, and Ibn al-Abbas al-Saghir, and Wali Allah Muhammad al-Qal'i the fragrance of his time, and Ibrahim al-Wajdiji, and Ibn Maluka, and other virtuous ones ((1). And Shaykh al-Mallali did not compose a chapter for talking about those who took from Imam al-Sanusi, and he is one of the eminent of his students, and the historian of his biography, and the collector of his reports and states. And among those who studied under Imam al-Sanusi while he was among his peers and the eminent of his time was the Imam, the knower of Allah, Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Burnusi al-Fasi known as (Zarruq), who died in the year (899 AH) despite his great prestige and high rank. He shared many of his teachers, and he explicitly stated studying under Imam al-Sanusi himself as transmitted by the historian, the scholar al-Tanbakti (2). And among the notables who met him and attended his general gatherings without directly reading upon him is Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Ali al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashi, who died in the year (938 AH). He chronicled him and his fragrant biography in his 'Thabat'. Famous, and among what he said: 'I met him, may Allah be pleased with him, and I attended his gathering that was packed with beneficiaries from students and the common people in his mosque near his house in Darb Masufa inside Tlemcen, may Allah protect it. I attended the Fatihah and the beginnings of Surat al-Baqarah being recited to him in the seven [modes], and other books, including al-Bukhari. It would be read to him in some of the gatherings I attended, and he would comment on its hadiths with speech that indicated his station in knowledge and worship. And other books of the gathering. And we attended - on the day we greeted him after we prayed 'Asr behind him - his 'Aqidah al-Sughra being recited before him. His students and a group of common people who were constant in his gathering would recite it by heart in a single voice, continuously, immediately after his salutation from the 'Asr prayer on Friday, as a continuous habit, while he was sitting in his prayer niche, facing towards remembrance.' And my eagerness: And he said: 'I was not destined to read upon him despite my desire for that because his students occupied all his sitting times. So much so that they would read upon him while one of them had a sandglass in his hand, and when it ran out, they would stop. I was hoping to read and waiting for a time, but death hastened to him - may Allah sanctify him - and I did not attain that wish.' (1) See 'Thabat Abi Ja'far al-Balawi' (p. 436). (2) See 'Thabat Abi Ja'far al-Balawi' (p. 437).
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the students and associates of Imam Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi. It begins by listing several scholars who studied with him: Ibn al-Hajj al-Baydari, Ibn al-Abbas al-Saghir, Wali Allah Muhammad al-Qal'i, Ibrahim al-Wajdiji, Ibn Maluka, and others. It then notes that Shaykh al-Mallali, one of his eminent students and his biographer, did not write a separate chapter about those who studied under al-Sanusi. The text then highlights a prominent figure, Imam Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Burnusi al-Fasi known as Zarruq (d. 899 AH), who was a contemporary and student of al-Sanusi and shared many teachers with him. The author then introduces Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Ali al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashi (d. 938 AH), who met al-Sanusi and attended his gatherings without directly reading under him. Al-Balawi's account, taken from his work 'Thabat', provides a vivid description: he attended al-Sanusi's mosque in Tlemcen, where the Quran was recited in the seven modes, and books like al-Bukhari were read with commentary. Most notably, al-Balawi witnessed al-Sanusi's 'Aqidah al-Sughra being recited from memory by students and laypeople in unison after the 'Asr prayer on Fridays. Al-Balawi expressed regret that he never had the chance to study directly under al-Sanusi due to the constant occupation of his students, and that death prevented him from fulfilling this wish. This passage is an important source for understanding al-Sanusi's teaching methods and the widespread reception of his creedal work.

زروق
أبو جعفر البلوي
ثبت

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's 'Aqidah al-Sughra was not only written but also memorized and recited collectively by students and laypeople after prayers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or study the 'Aqidah, is it merely an intellectual exercise, or does it become a living reality that you could proclaim from memory in a crowd? Would you be among those who make it a habit after prayer?
?
Al-Balawi deeply desired to read under al-Sanusi but was prevented by circumstances and death. What blessed knowledge have you postponed seeking? Will you take a concrete step this week to fill that gap?
?
The common people in the mosque joined the students in reciting the creed aloud. Is your aqeedah something you only hold in private, or do you verbalise it and share it with others, perhaps even in your family or community gatherings?

Encountering al-Sanusi's Teaching Sessions
A student narrates his encounter with al-Sanusi's classes and the custom of reciting the minor creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reverent atmosphere of al-Sanusi's teaching circle and the student's yearning to learn from him.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's teaching blended scholarship, devotion, and community ritual.

This passage offers a rare first-hand glimpse into the daily teaching practice of Imam al-Sanusi. We read a student's account of attending sessions filled with seekers and the common folk, witnessing the unique ritual recitation of al-Sanusi's minor creed. Beyond the descriptive details, the narrative reveals the deep respect and longing the student felt, which was unfulfilled due to al-Sanusi's death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Let the student's narrative flow naturally before you interpret.
Notice the mixture of scholarly and popular elements.
2
Identify the key activities
List what happens in the sessions: Quran recitation in seven modes, study of al-Bukhari, commentary on hadith, and the recitation of the minor creed after Asr on Fridays.
The minor creed recitation is a public display of learning.
3
Reflect on the student's regret
The student wanted to read directly with al-Sanusi but was prevented by his busy schedule. How does this highlight al-Sanusi's status?
The sandglass detail shows the structured use of time.
4
Consider the pedagogical implications
Think about how al-Sanusi’s method—combining formal study with public recitation and dhikr—created a holistic learning environment.
This narrative is not doctrinal but shows the living tradition.

The well-known, and among what he said: 'I met him, may Allah be pleased with him, and attended his session filled with seekers of knowledge and common people in his mosque near his house in Darb Masufa inside Tlemcen, may Allah protect it. I attended the Fatiha and the beginnings of Surat al-Baqara recited to him in the seven modes, and other books, including al-Bukhari, which was recited to him in some sessions I attended, and he spoke on its hadiths with speech that indicated his station in knowledge and worship and other books of the session. And we attended—on the day we greeted him after we prayed Asr behind him—his minor creed recited before him, his students and a group of commoners who always attended his session reciting it by heart in unison after his greeting from the Asr prayer on Friday, a continuous habit, while he was sitting in his prayer niche, facing the dhikr.' And his desire: And he said: 'I was not destined to read to him despite my desire for that, because his students occupied all his sitting times, so much so that they would read to him while a small bag was in the hand of one of them; when it was empty, it was cut off. I hoped to read and waited for a time, but death—may Allah sanctify him—hastened him, and I obtained none of that wish.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a first-hand biographical narrative from a student describing his encounters with Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by stating that the student met al-Sanusi and attended his teaching sessions, which were filled with both students and common people. The sessions took place in al-Sanusi's mosque near his home in Tlemcen. The student specifies that he attended the recitation of the Fatiha and early verses of Surat al-Baqara in the seven qira'at, as well as other books like Sahih al-Bukhari. Al-Sanusi would comment on the hadiths in a way that demonstrated his high level of knowledge and piety. The passage then describes a particular event: after praying Asr behind al-Sanusi, the student witnessed the recitation of al-Sanusi's minor creed ('aqida sughra) by the students and commoners, who recited it by heart in unison as a regular custom after Friday Asr prayer. Al-Sanusi would sit in his prayer niche engaged in dhikr. The student then expresses regret that he could not study directly with al-Sanusi because the advanced students occupied all his time; they would even read to him using a sandglass to measure time. Despite hoping for an opportunity, al-Sanusi died before the student could achieve that goal. The narrative emphasizes al-Sanusi's scholarly authority, the devotion of his followers, and the sanctity of his teaching setting.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage provides a theological proof or doctrinal argument.
Correction: The passage is a biographical anecdote, not a theological proof. It describes teaching practices and student experiences, not creedal reasoning.

Checkpoint
What did the students and commoners recite after the Friday Asr prayer in al-Sanusi's mosque?
A) The Fatiha and Surat al-Baqara
B) The minor creed (al-‘aqida al-sughra)
C) Sahih al-Bukhari
D) The seven modes of Quranic recitation

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi’s sessions combined rigorous Quranic study, hadith commentary, and communal dhikr, inspiring deep devotion in his followers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You stood in that mosque watching others recite the creed by heart while you only wished for a chance to learn directly from al-Sanusi. What is the 'wish' you have been postponing in your own journey of faith? Will you wait until it's too late, or will you act today?
?
The students measured their time with a sandglass, never wasting a moment. How do you measure your time with the Quran and the Prophet's hadith? Are you content with sporadic reading, or will you dedicate fixed, unhurried hours to learning your creed?
?
Al-Sanusi's session included both scholars and commonfolk. Has your pursuit of knowledge made you feel superior or separate from the general Muslims, or do you see yourself as part of the same community, all needing the same truths? Will you help others learn the minor creed as those students did, reciting together?
