كلمة عن كتاب شرح صفة الصغرى لا شكّ أنَّ «السنوسية الصغرى » هي لب لباب « السنوسيات » المباركة ، وليس لها ذاك الطولُ الذي يتعنَّى لأجله طالب علم ، فما الذي ألجأ الإمام السنوسي إلى اختصارها بـ « صغرى الصغرى » التي أيدينا ؟ بين إنّ الذي يقف على سبب ذلك يعلم حرص الإمام السنوسي البالغ في تفهيم معتقد أهل السنة ، وبذل الجهد منه في تنويع صياغته وحجمه لتحقيق هذه الغاية النبيلة ؛ فـ ( صغرى الصغري » ألّفت لوالد العلامة المؤرخ لسيرة الإمام السنوسي الشيخ الملالي ، قال في « المواهب القدسية » : ( قد كان وضعها لوالدي حفظه الله تعالى من كل آفة وبلية ، وأناله الدرجة العلية ، وذلك أنَّ والدي لما قرأ على الشيخ رضي الله عنه ( عقيدته الصغرى » وختمها عليه بالتفسير غير مرة . . رأى أنه قد ثقل عليه درسها وحفظها لكبره وكثرة همومه ، فطلب من الشيخ رضي الله عنه أن يجعل له عقيدة أصغر من « الصغرى » بحيث يمكنه درسها وحفظها ، فعمل له هذه العقيدة ، وكتبها له بخطه
A word about the book 'Explanation of the Small Creed' (Sharh Sifat al-Sughra). There is no doubt that the 'Sanusi al-Sughra' is the quintessence of the blessed 'Sanusiyyat' works, and it does not have that length which a student of knowledge would find burdensome. So what compelled Imam al-Sanusi to abbreviate it with the 'Sughra al-Sughra' which is in our hands? Know that the one who understands the reason for that knows the extreme concern of Imam al-Sanusi in making the creed of Ahl al-Sunna understood, and his effort in varying its formulation and size to achieve this noble goal. For the 'Sughra al-Sughra' was composed for the father of the scholar-historian of the biography of Imam al-Sanusi, Shaykh al-Mallali. He said in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya': 'He had written it for my father, may Allah preserve him from every affliction and calamity, and grant him the highest station. That is because when my father recited to the Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with him, his 'Small Creed' (al-Sughra) and completed it with commentary more than once, he saw that studying and memorizing it had become heavy upon him due to his old age and numerous preoccupations. So he asked the Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with him, to make for him a creed smaller than the 'Sughra', such that he could study and memorize it. So he wrote this creed for him and wrote it in his own handwriting.'
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative. It clarifies that Imam Sanusi's 'Sughra al-Sughra' is an even shorter version of his 'Sughra' creed, composed specifically for his father, who found the 'Sughra' too long to study and memorize due to his advanced age and many preoccupations. The editor cites al-Mallali's 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' to support this. The narrative shows Sanusi's dedication to making aqeedah accessible and his responsiveness to individual needs.

Key Terms
السنوسية الصغرى
صغرى الصغرى
المواهب القدسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Sanusi wrote multiple creeds without reason; in fact each served a specific pedagogical need.
Correction: The Sughra al-Sughra was written for a specific individual due to his personal circumstances, showing that Sanusi wrote his creeds with clear purposes.

Checkpoint
Why did Sanusi's father request an even shorter creed?
A) He wanted a different theological approach
B) The Sughra was too long for his old age and many preoccupations
C) He lost the original copy
D) He wanted to distribute it to students

Key Takeaway
The Sughra al-Sughra was composed by Imam Sanusi specifically to help his elderly father study and memorize creed despite his old age and many responsibilities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you neglected teaching or guiding a family member in matters of faith because it was inconvenient or time-consuming? How can you adopt Sanusi's sensitivity by tailoring religious instruction to their specific needs, even if it means creating a simpler version?
?
What 'preoccupations' in your life—work, worries, age, or distractions—have caused you to abandon or postpone deeper study of your creed? Are you willing to ask for a smaller, manageable portion rather than giving up entirely?
?
The father did not use his old age and many responsibilities as an excuse to stop learning; instead, he sought a smaller text. What one step can you take today to sustain your own learning of aqeedah, even if it means starting with the smallest step?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

3 min
Author Biography: Muhammad al-Sanusi
Colophon identifying author and death date.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity and historical context of the author Muhammad al-Sanusi as presented in the colophon.

Core Idea
The colophon identifies the author and his death date, grounding the text in history.

This lesson introduces the author of our text, Muhammad al-Sanusi. The colophon provides his full name, honorific titles, and death year. Understanding the author's background helps us appreciate the scholarly tradition from which this work emerges.

Guided Path
1
Read the colophon passage
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its structure. It begins with flowery titles, then the author's name, and ends with the death date.
2
Identify the author's full name
Find the name: Muhammad bin Yusuf bin Muhammad al-Sanusi al-Maliki. Note the lineage and the nisbah 'al-Sanusi' and 'al-Maliki'.
The titles before the name are not part of the name itself.
3
Note the death date
The death date is given as 895 AH (approximately 1490 CE). This places the author in the 9th century AH, a period of rich scholarly activity.
The abbreviation 'ت' stands for 'tawaffā' (he died).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تأليف مجيبي ما اندرس من الدين وناصر سنة سيد المرسلين [؟] مريم ربي عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بْن مجر السنوسي المالكي (ت ٨٩٥ هـ)
Authoring of the responder to what became extinct of the religion and the supporter of the sunnah of the master of the messengers [?] my Lord God Abdullah Muhammad bin Yusuf bin Muhammad al-Sanusi al-Maliki (d. 895 AH)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a colophon or title page identifying the author and work. It uses flowery titles: 'The responder to what became extinct of the religion and the supporter of the sunnah of the master of the messengers' before the author's name. The author is Muhammad bin Yusuf bin Muhammad al-Sanusi al-Maliki, with a death date of 895 AH (approximately 1490 CE). The name 'al-Sanusi' indicates his affiliation with the Sanusi order or lineage. The phrase 'مريم ربي' is unclear and may be a scribal error or invocation.

Key Terms

المالكي
ت ٨٩٥ هـ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'مجيبي ما اندرس من الدين' is part of the author's name.
Correction: It is an honorific title, not a component of his name. The name begins with 'عبد الله' (Abdullah).

Key Takeaway
Muhammad al-Sanusi, a Maliki scholar, died in 895 AH, and his colophon includes honorific titles that distinguish his role as a defender of the sunnah.

The Distinction Between Sayyid and Mawla
Sanusi explains why the Prophet is called sayyid before mawla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical reason why the Prophet is described as sayyid (master) before mawla (supporter) in Sunni creed.

Core Idea
Sayyid is the one we turn to first; mawla is the one who helps afterwards.

In this passage, Sanusi explains that the order of these titles is not arbitrary but follows a logical sequence of action: one first seeks refuge from a sayyid, and then receives support from a mawla. Understanding this distinction deepens our appreciation of the Prophet's role as both refuge and helper.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the definitions of sayyid and mawla.
2
Identify Definitions
Sanusi defines sayyid as the one to whom one turns for refuge in every important matter, and mawla as the supporter. Note these definitions.
3
Grasp the Logical Sequence
Understand that turning for refuge (to sayyid) logically precedes receiving support (from mawla). This is the core reason for the order.
The sequence is: first seek refuge, then receive help.
4
Apply to the Prophet
See how this applies to the Prophet: he is the refuge and supporter in this world (through guidance) and in the Hereafter (through intercession and status).
The Prophet is both sayyid and mawla for all creatures.
5
Reflect on the Prayer
The passage ends with a prayer asking Allah for benefit through the Prophet's status. Consider its significance as a request for both worldly and otherworldly help.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قدَّمنا في أصل العقيدة وصفه عليه الصلاة والسلام بالسيد على وصفه بالمولى ؛ لأنَّ السيّد هو الذي يُفزَعُ إليهِ في كلِّ مُهِمِّ والمولى هو الناصرُ ، ولا شكّ أنَّ الفزعَ في المُهِمِّ إلى السيّدِ يكونُ أوَّلاً ، ونصرتَهُ لِمَنْ فَزِعَ إليه في نيلِ مُهِمِّهِ تكون ثانياً بعد فزعِهِ إِليه ، ولا شكّ أنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ مَفزَعُ الخلائق ، وناصرهم في الدنيا ؛ بَيَّنَ لهم مِنْ طريقِ النجاة ، وعلَّمَهُم مِنْ أنواع الهداياتِ ، حتى تركهم على المَحَجَّةِ البيضاء التي لا غبار عليها ، ومَفزَعُهُم وناصرُهُم في الآخرة ؛ إذ له المقام المحمود هناك ، والشفاعة المتكثرة المشفّعة ، والمقالة المسموعة ، والسؤالُ المُعْطَى ، والجاه الأعظم ، والمنزلة العليا ، نسأل الله تعالى أن يَهَب لنا نصيباً وافراً مِنَ النفع بسيادتِهِ وجاهه الأعظم دنيا وأخرى
And we only gave precedence in the foundation of the creed to describing him, peace and blessings be upon him, as sayyid over describing him as mawla, because the sayyid is the one to whom one turns for refuge in every important matter, and the mawla is the supporter. There is no doubt that turning for refuge in important matters to the sayyid comes first, and his support for the one who turns to him for refuge in obtaining his important matter occurs secondarily after his turning to him. There is no doubt that he, peace and blessings be upon him, is the refuge of creatures and their supporter in this world: he showed them the path of salvation and taught them the types of guidance until he left them upon the clear path which has no dust upon it. And he is their refuge and supporter in the Hereafter, for he has the Praiseworthy Station there, and the abundant intercession that is accepted, and the listened-to speech, and the granted request, and the greatest status, and the lofty rank. We ask Allah Almighty to grant us an abundant share of benefit through his sayyidship and his greatest status, in this world and the Hereafter.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage explains the reason for ordering the titles 'sayyid' and 'mawla' when describing the Prophet (PBUH). Sanusi begins by stating that in the foundation of the creed, they gave precedence to describing the Prophet as sayyid over mawla. He then defines the two terms: sayyid is the one to whom one turns for refuge in every important matter, while mawla is the supporter. The logical order is that turning for refuge (to the sayyid) comes first, and support (from the mawla) comes second after turning to him. Sanusi then applies this to the Prophet: he is the refuge and supporter of all creatures in this world through his guidance, and in the Hereafter through his Praiseworthy Station and intercession. The passage concludes with a prayer for benefit from the Prophet's status.

Key Terms
السيد
المولى
المقام المحمود
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The order of titles 'sayyid' and 'mawla' is arbitrary.
Correction: Sanusi demonstrates that 'sayyid' precedes 'mawla' because turning for refuge logically comes before receiving support.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi give precedence to describing the Prophet as 'sayyid' over 'mawla'?
A) Because 'sayyid' is a more honorable title.
B) Because turning for refuge to the sayyid logically precedes receiving support from the mawla.
C) Because the Prophet preferred to be called sayyid.
D) Because 'mawla' implies a lower status.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet is our master to whom we turn first and our supporter who aids us, reflecting the logical sequence of seeking refuge then receiving help.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a crisis, do you instinctively turn to the Prophet as your sayyid—the one you flee to—or do you rely on your own plans and efforts? What would it look like to make him your first refuge, not an afterthought?
?
The Prophet has supported you by showing the path of salvation and teaching guidance. Are you actively seeking his teachings in the Quran and Sunnah, or have you neglected his guidance? What one step can you take today to follow his path more closely?
?
You believe the Prophet has the greatest status and intercession in the Hereafter. Yet, do you live in a way that shows you are counting on his intercession? If you were to die tonight, would you be confident that you have benefited from his sayyidship? Commit to one action that strengthens your connection to him.
